#### Geography for ICSE Middle School

Dorothy M. Noronha

Nelson Petrie

As per National Curriculum Framework (NCF) 2023

Exploring and interacting with the natural and human environment

Developing an interdisciplinary perspective

rooted in disciplinary knowledge

Appreciating cultures and ways of life of people around the world

Making informed judgements at local, national and international levels

##### In this book:

Recognize the physical features of an area

Identify human relationships with the natural environment

Enhance geographical concepts and skills

Learn the contributions of other disciplines

through an interdisciplinary approach

Create and think critically to form informed opinions

Go beyond with discovery and research-based activities to enhance concepts

Learn about building a sustainable society

# Preface

Voyage is a series of three geography books for classes 6–8 and is completely aligned to the National Curriculum Framework for School Education 2023 and the latest curriculum released by the Council for the Indian School Certificate Examinations (CISCE).

The series promotes an understanding of the different elements of the physical environment that affect life on earth. The title 'Voyage' represents the quest that students will embark on to explore the continents of the world. This will enable them to have a better understanding of the interrelationship that exists between human beings and the environment. The exercises and activities given in this series are also designed to achieve the same goal.

The book for class 8 deals with topographical sheets to identify landforms and settlement patterns. It includes geographical concepts such as population, migration and urbanization. This book has a detailed study of Asia and a section devoted to India. Topics on natural and man-made disasters and disaster management have also been included. Certain topics have been included for the sake of continuity and a more comprehensive understanding of a concept.

We would like to thank our well-wishers for their help, encouragement and goodwill during the making of this series. We also sincerely thank the editors at Oxford University Press India for their co-operation, commitment, hard work and patience.

Dorothy Martha Noronha

##### National Curriculum Framework for School Education 2023 (NCF 2023)

Nelson Petrie

The study of Social Sciences in general, and geography in particular, is essential to develop a multidisciplinary perspective. The study of geography is essential as it studies the physical features of an area, and the relationship humans have with their natural environment, thereby expanding their horizons and opening their minds to new possibilities. Equipped with the methods of observing and interpreting the human world, learners lead their own lives while contributing to society. The series includes the United Nation's Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs) in each chapter, which identifies Education for Sustainable Development as a key facilitator in building a sustainable society, that protects the present and looks towards the future. The series also aims to portray the importance of Indian context, Indian thought, and Indian Knowledge and Knowledge Systems through the Knowledge of India feature box.

## Key Features

Voyage covers the topics of physical and world geography in a manner that facilitates a sound understanding of geographical concepts and the different regions of the world.

##### Learning Tools

Learning Outcomes in each chapter which are measurable

Recall assesses learners previous knowledge

- Summary Flow Charts present the key points of the chapter in a structured format to help with easy recapitulation.

- Important Terms help explain key terms in a simple way.

#### Assessment Tools

• Exercises gradually prepare students for the board examinations.

Sample Term Papers facilitate quick revision.

Worksheets and Map Practice provide additional practice.

### Additional Information

Did You Know? provides interesting information to pique the interest of students

- Quick Facts provide useful information related to the topic.

- Websites provided at the end of each chapter encourage learners to acquire knowledge and awareness beyond the syllabus

##### Extended Learning

The following elements in each chapter help develop essential skills.

Discuss helps develop observation, listening and communication skills.

Think and Answer encourages critical thinking and learning.

- Subject Integration suggested by the syllabus provides linkages between geography and other subjects.

• transactional Processes in each chapter, mentioned in CISCE syllabus, to understand the concepts.

Source-based Questions in the form of picture study and case-based questions assesses the analytical skills of the learner.

• Illustrated Stories use captivating narrative and vibrant artwork to bring to life people and events from history.

• HOTS Question to develop the higher order functions of the brain like application and analysis.

- Map Work enhances map-marking skills.

• Values and Life Skills facilitate introspection and reasoning skills.

• Biography introduces learners to new personalities.

Cross-Curricular Connect enable an interdisciplinary approach to learning key geographical concepts.

Let's Do Something provides ample opportunities to extend the learning beyond the classroom, apply the acquired knowledge and provide hands-on experience through various activities and project work.

### Support Material

Teacher's Handbook containing lesson-pl answer keys, addict questions, a glossary and model test papers with answer keys.

• Oxford Educate containing an e-book with interactive teaching tools like animations, lesson plans, worksheets, answer keys, interactive games, quizzes and more.

An easy-to-use Dynamic Question Bank used to create a variety of assessment papers.

### National Curriculum Framework for School Education 2023

Voyage is completely aligned to the visions of the National Curriculum Framework 2023. It achieves this through the following features:

• Competencies: The exercises, activities and the worksheets have been tagged with the relevant competencies mentioned in the document.

• 21st century skills: Activities and exercises are designed to enhance various learning skills like critical thinking, communication, creativity, etc. and are tagged to each area of assessment.

• Knowledge of India: This feature enhances rootedness in India and instils pride in the Indian system.

- Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs): Through this section, the series aims to create awareness about several of the Sustainable Development Goals set by the United Nations.

• Digital Integration: Digital tools are integrated to aid and enhance the learning-teaching experience.

##### Skill: Communication

You studied topographical sheets in class 7. How is colour used on topographical maps? Discuss.

##### TOPOGRAPHICAL MAPS

These are large-scale maps that show both natural and man-made features. In a topographical map, the shape of the land is generally shown by contour lines. A contour line is an imaginary line that connects all points having the same height above mean sea level.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a4b7fd0d-4e28-4868-9ad0-96bc9bf9981e/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_104_1181_605_1578.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2Fcba5c7e190fc5118fdec79be0a860e924ea4f407df6916a1246342b322ce7edf" alt="Image" width="42%" /></div>


##### Contour lines

Since a topographical map is drawn provide detailed information of a small area a set of arbitrary lines, instead of latitude and longitudes are provided to help local a particular feature or place. These lines a known as eastings and northings. These line form a network or a grid of squares.

A topographical map is also called a top sheet. We read a topo sheet from the extrem south-west grid or the grid at the bottom corner.

##### Features of the Grid System

- The lines that run vertically are called eastings, while those that run horizontal are called northings.

Eastings and northings cross each other form a square known as a grid square.

The extreme south-west grid, or the one the bottom left corner, is the starting point or reference point.

The numerical value of eastings increases eastwards beginning from the south-we corner. Similarly, the numerical value northings increases northwards.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a4b7fd0d-4e28-4868-9ad0-96bc9bf9981e/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_118_168_448_480.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2Faec5e40ed0088986056b248245fa21867b630f95876f0dc824179727466a76d7" alt="Image" width="27%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a4b7fd0d-4e28-4868-9ad0-96bc9bf9981e/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_chart_box_111_524_458_829.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2Fd4f164bd47e52f4eea70af1861b3eda07f0597fb0179611fc5764696829282a8" alt="Image" width="29%" /></div>


When referring to a grid, eastings are always stated first.

Eastings and northings are always given in two-digit numbers. For example, 01, 02, 03... 98, 99. Even 0 is read as 00.

Eastings and northings on a topo sheet drawn on a scale of 1:50,000 are always 2 cm apart, which means they represent a distance of 1 km on the ground. So, the area of 2 cm × 2 cm on the map represents 1 km × 1 km on the ground.

There are two types of grid references—(i) the four-figure reference and (ii) the six-figure reference. The four-figure reference is used to locate places that fall within the numbered grid square, for example, the grid reference for the shaded square in the four-figure diagram is 1705.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a4b7fd0d-4e28-4868-9ad0-96bc9bf9981e/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_570_730_950_805.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2Fa4bb1e5d4841752a7f7c0d10aabd5cb68177b93a457c28e9494b02219e950004" alt="Image" width="31%" /></div>


A large-scale map can show many more features than a small-scale map.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a4b7fd0d-4e28-4868-9ad0-96bc9bf9981e/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_43_881_1071_1539.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2F0278e4ee5874a0074435ff37db72111b48f70ad72c83da8e0cf3763b53099e2f" alt="Image" width="86%" /></div>


A part of a topographical map showing eastings and northings

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a4b7fd0d-4e28-4868-9ad0-96bc9bf9981e/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_chart_box_118_104_643_599.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A30Z%2F-1%2F%2Fa33e1e23575167aa9c96cc42afb33c878d386623f5215da2342c77c797313c5c" alt="Image" width="44%" /></div>


## A four-figure grid reference

The six-figure grid reference is used to locate an object, such as wells, post offices, milestones or temples, within a grid square with greater accuracy. In the six-figure grid reference, the first three figures are the castings while the last three are the northings. To get the six-figure grid reference, you need to divide the grid square on the top of sheet into ten equal parts vertically and horizontally. These figures will give you the third figure for the eastings and the sixth figure for the northings. For example, the grid reference for the church in the six-figure diagram is 213052.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a4b7fd0d-4e28-4868-9ad0-96bc9bf9981e/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_chart_box_108_1085_635_1570.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A30Z%2F-1%2F%2F1e54d1fbc6867b58245ca548e28aa61553c134118e248d637d1e9d4468dcfdd9" alt="Image" width="44%" /></div>


A church shown with the help of a six-figure grid reference

## REPRESENTATION OF RELIEF OR ELEVATION ON A TOPO SHEET USING CONTOURS

Several methods are used to depict physical features on a topo sheet. Using contours is the most common method of showing religion or elevation on topo sheets. We have already read that a contour line connects all points having the same height above mean sea level.

On a topo sheet there are several such lines with specific numbers that indicate the height of all the places connected by these lines. The numerical value of a contour line is different from the one above or below it. The difference in height between two adjacent contour lines is known as the contour interval. It is also known as the Vertical Interval (VI). The distance between any two adjacent contour lines is called the Horizontal Equivalence (HE). The Horizontal Equivalent is calculated with the help of the scale of the map. The value of the HE is less when the slope is steep and more when it is gentle. Contour lines of the topographical maps made by the Survey of India are always measured in metres.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a4b7fd0d-4e28-4868-9ad0-96bc9bf9981e/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_667_982_734_1050.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A30Z%2F-1%2F%2Fb9c2c17a355b600ff5757a893a512d4b3003ed74152a5755dc83caba79165de8" alt="Image" width="5%" /></div>


The topo sheets prepared by Survey of India are in three main groups:

The quarter-inch sheet has a scale of 1:250,000 or 1 cm:2.5 km.

The million sheet, where the scale of the sheet is 1:1,000,000 or 1 cm:10 km.

#### Quick Facts

The one-inch sheet has a scale of 1:50,000 or 2 cm:1 km.

Some basic characteristics of contour line are:

- Contour lines are drawn at fixed vertices intervals, for example, 20 m. These intervals on the map will not change. They depen

on the scale of the map and the range of elevation in the area of the map.

- Contour lines do not intersect one another. They could meet and touch each other, but not cross one another.

- On a topographical map, every fifth line is accentuated or drawn thick. It is known as the contour index.

The spacing between contour lines determines the nature of the slope. If contour lines are drawn close together, it indicates that the slope of the land is steep. If they are drawn far apart, it indicates that the land is gentle. Contour lines drawn at equal intervals indicate that the slope is neither steep nor gentle. Such a slope is called a uniform slope.

### IDENTIFICATION OF SIMPLE LANDFORMS

##### Gentle Slope and Steep Slope

In a steep slope, the contours are drawn close to one another while on a gentle slope, they are wide apart.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//51b61dd8-e001-45bb-ac6d-7e59d81df239/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_12_969_526_1387.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A25Z%2F-1%2F%2F025944f4c84b57443b8565fd4bcb7002985b902d90c8c46913d29e8655b53dcd" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">A gentle slope and a steep slope</div> </div>


##### Plateau

A plateau or a tableland is an uplifted piece of flat land with slopes on all sides. On a contour map, plateaus are marked by contour lines very close to each other on all sides while there are none or very few lines at the centre.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//51b61dd8-e001-45bb-ac6d-7e59d81df239/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_562_359_1092_679.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A25Z%2F-1%2F%2F2180e8f266abeb3765af83384e4869bba927afd56efa7ac0f1284109d0aab3ed" alt="Image" width="44%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">▲ A plateau</div> </div>


##### Conical Hill

A conical hill is simply a low-elevation hill in the shape of a cone with uniform steepness on all sides. The contour lines of a conical hill are evenly spaced in almost concentric circles.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//51b61dd8-e001-45bb-ac6d-7e59d81df239/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_552_953_1082_1384.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A25Z%2F-1%2F%2F689e2ec1cd15781e1e7e0a5a81acf3aadb830f0e84ac23bb95213c57f8be277b" alt="Image" width="44%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">▲ A conical hill</div> </div>


##### Ridge

A ridge is a long and narrow elevation which has steep slopes on either side and stands out from the surrounding lowlands. It also acts as a watershed for rivers that flow down narrow valleys on both of its sides. A ridge could also have several peaks of various elevations. The contours of a ridge are oval with contours close to each other indicating steepness.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//51b61dd8-e001-45bb-ac6d-7e59d81df239/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_133_403_621_879.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A26Z%2F-1%2F%2F53919bb7e67b4efb7d260919d2329e437d6f9605a75d6b709583c618beb61e8a" alt="Image" width="41%" /></div>


##### ▲ A ridge

##### Saddie

A saddle is a shallow depression at a high elevation between two peaks or ridges. The depression is formed by streams or by glaciers flowing close to each other. A saddle need not have a river or stream flowing through it.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//51b61dd8-e001-45bb-ac6d-7e59d81df239/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_171_1144_595_1528.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A26Z%2F-1%2F%2F2b08ef5385ade29a1e89a4b7b6ad8cd6f660d293b961b4c766e55075e247fee5" alt="Image" width="35%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">▲ A saddle</div> </div>


##### cliff

A cliff is a vertical or near vertical feature. The landform rises vertically from the lower ground. On a contour map, contour lines are very close together a merge into a single line. In other words, what contour lines overlap, this indicates a cliff.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//51b61dd8-e001-45bb-ac6d-7e59d81df239/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_672_280_1181_774.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A26Z%2F-1%2F%2Fa22dfa4f38922d86ce17f9d48b306b52fdb0d19664767d4f0d9c1484ef89dd4d" alt="Image" width="42%" /></div>


A cliff

#### Waterfall

A waterfall is formed when there is a sudden drop in the river valley. It is like a cliff when the drop is almost perpendicular.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//51b61dd8-e001-45bb-ac6d-7e59d81df239/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_716_965_1180_1550.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2F47f95286dccad77e45d781b4c5edf1871f6a659416e7bb997bdac68b55e5a792" alt="Image" width="38%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">▲ A waterfall</div> </div>


Waterfalls are formed in the upper regions of river valleys. When contours on a map are very close to one another or sometimes touch each other as they cross a river or stream, it indicates the presence of a waterfall.

##### V-shaped Valley

V-shaped valleys are found in the upper course of a river where the slopes on either side of the river are steep. A V-shaped valley is easily identified on a contour map with the contour lines close to each other and a very dominant V.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//51b61dd8-e001-45bb-ac6d-7e59d81df239/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_9_574_554_1124.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2Fabf25617259772781a19dc22d687f858669d3ec232541321a2e9614d5553d6fd" alt="Image" width="45%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">A V-shaped valley</div> </div>


##### U-shaped Valley

U-shaped valleys are found in regions where the action of ice (or glaciers) has widened the valleys so that the valleys take the shape of a 'U'. These are also found in the lower regions of a river where the erosion of valley walls by the river widens the valley to make them look U-shaped. The contour lines of these valleys are bent in a distinct U shape.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//51b61dd8-e001-45bb-ac6d-7e59d81df239/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_610_108_1080_578.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2F18d7bdea1a8a4c1deedb4858ddb8e0e01874614663da95ca3fad912b4cc51f24" alt="Image" width="39%" /></div>


▲ A U-shaped valley

##### Col

A col is formed when the land has been cut considerably between two streams in a watershed. A col can be identified by a drop in height of the contours.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//51b61dd8-e001-45bb-ac6d-7e59d81df239/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_585_820_1126_1500.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2Fc0d562e5fee0c7cdbf0e6be9cb2dbaa767d09fc8371658274d359de7532f75f2" alt="Image" width="45%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">▲ A col</div> </div>


##### Pass

Passes are low valleys or openings lying between two peaks in a range of bills. A pass is also indicated by a drop in height of contours.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//51b61dd8-e001-45bb-ac6d-7e59d81df239/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_169_208_621_821.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2Ff32fcd3147671112f4369c85c9fdda19ddc21222d433256b293e2e03ea735dc9" alt="Image" width="37%" /></div>


▲ A pass

##### Gap

A gap is a low-lying depression or a valley which cuts through a range of hills. It is often occupied by a river.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//51b61dd8-e001-45bb-ac6d-7e59d81df239/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_118_1000_589_1612.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F1544be0fbf5f4bde4e8c1620dc6cbed21b91c87374891a216cf962f25e4ab042" alt="Image" width="39%" /></div>


## SETTLEMENT PATTERNS UN TOPO SHEETS

Settlements are groups of houses, usually villages or towns, where people live. This of settlements depends on the available of roads, railways, hospitals, police stations, administrative buildings, rest houses and on. Settlements grow over a period of many factors determine the location and type of settlements:

Settlements grow in flat areas and the land is cultivable. Settlements grow on steep hillsides or marshy lands

Settlements grow in places where water available in plenty for both agricultural and domestic purposes. Settlements, therefore also grow on the confluence of rivers, the banks of rivers.

Settlements also thrive on a plate because of the flat surface of the plate and the availability of land for cultivation

They develop and grow in places where climate is suitable or pleasant to live. Extremely hot, cold, wet or dry places not attractive settlement sites.

Settlements are formed where there  $ {}^{1} $ prospects for employment. Mines are industries in the area are potential source of employment and encourage the growth of settlements. Such places are usually no places of abundant raw materials for growth of industries.

• They develop in places that are east accessible by various kinds of road rivers, and railway lines. Easy access to an from the settlements will allow movement of people and goods from one place another.

A settlement can be permanent or temporal. Settlements that are constructed and occupy for a short time are called temporal.

settlements. Temporary settlements are built by people engaged in hunting and gathering, shifting cultivation and transhumance. Tents and huts are the most common forms of shelter in temporary settlements. At times, a temporary settlement is built next to a construction site, such as a bridge or a flyover. However, this form of temporary settlement is usually found in an urban area. A temporary settlement can become permanent with time. In permanent settlements, people build permanent houses. In the course of time, several such structures are constructed and a settlement develops. The availability of water and land for cultivation are important reasons for the growth of such settlements. In addition, there is availability of communication lines such as roads and railways and other facilities such as a police station, a post office, a hospital or a health centre, a market, etc.

##### Types of Settlements

A topo sheet has several settlement patterns. The three main types of settlement patterns are as follows:

##### Nucleated settlements

In nucleated settlements, buildings and huts are in a compact cluster.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//51b61dd8-e001-45bb-ac6d-7e59d81df239/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_20_1020_509_1495.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2Fad2af3520ee71e6d2164cc39217fa72c3008f031f88e58fe29af52d61d575c87" alt="Image" width="41%" /></div>


▲ A nucleated settlement

These settlements are usually found in plains or valleys. This kind of settlement indicates that the community lives where the land is fertile and suitable for agriculture. Nucleated settlements generally have a well-knit and large community. Apart from houses, essential facilities like hospitals, police stations, post offices, schools, and administrative buildings are found. Nucleated settlements are also known as clustered settlements.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//51b61dd8-e001-45bb-ac6d-7e59d81df239/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_558_432_1095_532.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2F8cd733ec8a6b0001c70788724627557aed52c50be9a0e0d1eca5170edba2436c" alt="Image" width="45%" /></div>


##### Think and Answer

Skill: Critical Thinking

Why do you think nucleated settlements are found in plains and valleys?

##### Linear settlements

Linear settlements are those that are formed in a line. Houses, shops, dhabas, petrol pumps and garages develop along the sides of roads, railway lines or river banks. Gradually, these linear settlements grow in size.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//51b61dd8-e001-45bb-ac6d-7e59d81df239/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_581_870_1095_1364.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2F0b38d4fde61ca832ee9502483ca36a53150d7617f5dca5d923c93f0b0116b6e9" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">A linear settlement</div> </div>


These settlements gradually develop into trading centres. If such a settlement is near a railway track, and over a period of time there

is a need for a railway station, then it becomes a railway stop. When located on main roads, such settlements become important stops for travellers as dhabas, tyre and car repairing shops and petrol pumps are set up. On rivers and coasts, they become places where boats can unload goods and passengers.

##### Scattered settlements

Scattered settlements are also known as dispersed settlements. Houses or huts in this type of settlement are far apart from one another. On the map, such a settlement is indicated by long distances between houses. Areas of scattered settlement indicate a sparse population and the absence of proper roads. Houses or huts are usually connected by cart tracks or paths. In dispersed settlements, cattle rearing is common as each household has cattle that are allowed to graze in the open fields. Also, the land is not very fertile to support large populations.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//acfdc676-e99e-43a9-9da3-b67356389eb5/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_164_883_680_1081.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2F47efe0da16f2a7eea6d22556ca6886d06bdf7418334cf22617a39d0d511ec8e9" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">▲ A scattered settlement</div> </div>


##### TRANSPORT AND COMMUNICATION

On a topographical map, you will notice some black lines that cross the map. These lines are symbols of roadways and railway tracks and indicate the type of communication in the area. They depict the various modes of transport being used in the area.

On a topo sheet, there are metalled and unmetalled roads. Vehicles such as trucks, buses, cars, jeeps, and other modern means of transport move over metalled roads. There are also cart tracks, pack tracks and footpaths, which are unmetalled roads. C� tracks and pack tracks connect small villages settlements in rural areas, while footpaths normally found through hilly terrain, which is inaccessible even by carts. Pack tracks too, are found in hilly and rough terrains where goods are loaded on the backs of mules and ponies and taken from one remote village to another.

The layout of roads and railways is planned according to the relief and drainage of the area. The abundance of bridges indicates the many streams that exist in the area. Tunnel and cuttings indicate hilly terrain. Rail routes are planned through areas that provide a little gradient as possible since trains have haul heavy goods. To avoid steep gradient tunnels and cuttings are made for railways to run through. Embankments are raised constructions built on the ground. They are often used to prevent floodwater from entering the land. Roads and railways are built on these embankments since the ground below is too soft to support a road or a railway track. Causeways are also built over small streams or metalled roads.

In India, there are three types of railway gauge —broad, metre and narrow. Sometime broad gauge lines are indicated as double track or single track. On the double track, trains on two sets of railway lines at all times, which on single tracks, trains ply only on one set railway lines at regulated intervals. In India the metre gauge is being phased out gradual and is now found mostly in the extreme eastern corner of the country. Narrow gauge is confined to popular hill stations such as Darjiling in West Bengal and Shimla Himachal Pradesh. Communication at transport lines indicates the importance of place. When many roads and railways converge in a village or a town, it indicates

importance of a place. It could be for several reasons, such as the economic activity of the region or the region could be a tourist hot spot, or it could be because of the presence of industries and factories leading to plenty of job opportunities.

Airports are also an important form of travel and communication, but airports are confined to large cities only. The conventional sign of an aeroplane indicates the presence of an airport or an airstrip.

##### Conventional Symbols of a map

The symbols and signs which are accepted by all are known as conventional symbols. The various tools in the conventional symbols are the combination of dots, lines, colours and alphabets. They can be used to depict features like cities, roads and railways.

##### Conventional signs and symbols

- A variety of colourful signs and symbols are used to show natural and man-made features on maps.

- These signs and symbols give plenty of information and are simple to draw and understand.

Some of these symbols are internationally recognized as they have been determined by convention, i.e., these symbols have been agreed upon and accepted internationally. Therefore, they are also called conventional signs and symbols.

People of any country, who are familiar with these symbols, can easily interpret maps of other countries as well.

### HOW TO READ AND INTERPRET A TOPOGRAPHICAL MAP

A topographical map, a part of which you see on page 18, provides a lot of information of both natural and man-made features. Natural features means physical features such as hills, valleys, ridges, plains, plateaus, depressions and so forth, while man-made features include objects such as canals, dams, bridges, railway lines, cart tracks, highways, buildings and so on. You have already learnt about the colours and conventional signs and symbols used in a topographical map in the previous class.

These are the aspects you should bear in mind as you study a topographical map:

- The sheet number: Each sheet has a number printed on it. The topo sheet extract you see in this chapter is part of the sheet number G43S7. This number refers to a specific geographical area in India. Sheet G43S7 shows a part of Banas Kantha district in Gujarat.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//acfdc676-e99e-43a9-9da3-b67356389eb5/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_chart_box_90_115_1190_1551.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2Fdd633c9e9662b7ded1902e963c69fc9c4775992679ef60b3f096efc9da0affef" alt="Image" width="92%" /></div>


- Scale: The scale of the sheet is found at the bottom. The scale is not the same for all maps. There are some maps that show a scale of 1:10,000,000. The map G43S7 has a scale of 1:50,000. It means that if you measure 1 cm on the map, it actually corresponds to 50,000 cm on the ground. In other words, the scale of this map is 2 cm:1 km, which implies that every 2 cm on the map corresponds to 1 km on the ground.

Grid: The topographical maps have grid lines in red, which help in locating places easily. These lines are called eastings and northings. If you measure each grid square, you will find it is  $ 2 \, cm \times 2 \, cm $. On the actual ground, remember that each grid is  $ 1 \, km \times 1 \, km $ or the area of each grid square is  $ 1 \, sq. \, km $.

- Direction on map sheet: The top half of a topographical map is always the north, the bottom half is the south, your right hand is the east and your left hand is the west. The south-west corner is from where the eastings and the northings are read.

• Eastings and northings: The map extract shows a region between eastings 37 to 46 and northings 89 to 00. These are very important numbers to remember before you embark on your map-reading exercise.

Four-figure and six-figure grid squares: Four-figure grid references will have four digits and six-figure grid references will have six digits. The area of each square is  $ 2 \, \text{cm} \times 2 \, \text{cm} $ or  $ 1 \, \text{km} \times 1 \, \text{km} $ on the ground. For example, the area enclosed by eastings 38 and 42 and by northings 94 and 98 is  $ 4 \times 4 $ (length by breadth) sq km = 16 sq. km. The village of Manpuriya is located in the four-figure grid square 4197 and Karja is located in four figure grid square 3994. In the six-figure grid square 413978, a temple is given while in grid 398951 conventional

sign ( $ \Delta $) of a triangulated station that indicates the height of a place from the sea level is given. A conventional sign of a survey tree is located on an island in Banas River in 440941.

Legend and keys: Legends contain conventional signs and symbols in the form of keys. Before you proceed to interpret the map, familiarize yourself with these signs and symbols which help you to interpret the map more accurately and infer the required information about relief, drainage, land use, transport, settlements, etc. They provide all the vital information that is required to enable the reader to interpret the map correctly.

##### HOTS Question

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//acfdc676-e99e-43a9-9da3-b67356389eb5/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_1032_605_1102_666.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2Fb6676eea4b89d1db1bb467910741c3ffb7963bdbd71baf6acb52c78ef85db220" alt="Image" width="5%" /></div>


What will happen if you do not know how to read the map legend or key?

• Contour Interval: The Contour Interval is 20 m. This means that the vertical distance between two consecutive contour lines is 20 m. It is also known as the Vertical Interval (V.I). In all topo sheets of 1:50,000 the V.I. is constant.

- Spot heights: These indicate the actual elevation of a spot above mean sea level. Spot heights on a topo sheet are shown by a small black dot with a number indicating its height. There are a number of spot heights shown on this map. For example, .522 (grid reference 425943) on the western half of the map is one such spot height.

- Triangulated stations: Another indicator of heights on maps is a triangulated station. A triangulated station is also a specific spot on a topo sheet that indicates the height of a place. Such a spot is called a station and is located in the highest region of the area. It is indicated on the map with a small

triangle $\Delta$ followed by the number. There are a number of triangulated stations on this map, such as $\Delta$ 268 (grid reference 399951).

- Contour Index: Note every fifth contour line. It is bolder than the other lines. This is the Contour Index for easy identification of contour lines. In grid square 4295, the Contour Index 400 is accentuated.

- On this map, there are several places with letters DEP encircled within a contour line. The letters stand for DEPRESSION. It indicates land in this area is at a lower level than the surrounding area.

#### Knowledge of India

The National Atlas Organization was created in 1956. The first National Atlas in Hindi, Bharat: Rastriya Atlas, was published in 1957.

The main water body that flows right across the map extract is the Banas River. The tributary that joins it is the Balaram Nadi. Note the two arrows that are shown in Banas River and Balaram Nadi. The arrows indicate the directions in which the rivers are flowing. In Banas River, the arrow points to the south-east direction and in Balaram Nadi, the arrow points to the north-west direction. The place where the two rivers, Banas River and Balaram Nadi meet is called a confluence (Grid Reference 4292).

Dry and wet streams: On the map there are streams that are black in colour and others that are blue in colour. The black streams are dry and have no water, while the blue streams (including the Banas River and the Balaram Nadi) are blue since they have water.

There are several types of contour features in the map as well. In grid square 42 in the map as well. In grid square 43 in the map as well. In grid square 44 in the map as well. In grid slope or escarpment; there is a steep slope or escarpment; grid square 4395, there is a saddle or a pits in grid square 4295, there is a ridge or watershed. Spot Height 542 is a peak or the highest point.

The map has two dominant colours. These are green and white. The green contains vegetation, chiefly forests. No the type of forests indicated on the map. There are three types of forests—dense jungle, dense mixed jungle and fairy dense jungle. The white portion is barren land. No crops are grown on this land. Part of it is also open scrub. Most of the hill terrain is also barren. Notice the hill with a spot height .542 in grid square 4294. There is a patch of white. It indicates that the forest has been cut and deforestation has taken place.

- Man-made objects: Man-made objects include settlements, roads, cart track temples, chattris, etc. in this map.

• Settlements come in different patterns: nucleated, scattered and linear. On the map, the pattern of settlement in grid square 4099 is nucleated or compact. In grid square 4392, settlements are scattered. Remember, settlements are always shown by red squares. A single square indicates a single hut, such as the one in grid 4590 where the squares are separated. The largest settlement in the map is Khara.

Transport: All the settlements on the map are connected by cart tracks. The broker red line from Chekhla to Jyol are pack tracks

##### Biography

The first contour lines were drawn by Charles Hutton, a British mathematician. He carried out a survey of a Scottish peak called Schiehallion in 1774, which is known to be the first time he used contour lines. The map did not survive, but Hutton's original charts and tables of survey points were fortunately, not lost to history. It is said that the invention of the contour lines to measure the height of Schiehallion was originally not the objective of Hutton; it was actually to weigh the mountain.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//788be9b8-e576-44f2-8046-3654d709a96e/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_896_407_1124_603.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A25Z%2F-1%2F%2Fd20475a3d115096120789fbb43a16d3127875435082fe96e42e433899db55460" alt="Image" width="19%" /></div>


Interpreting Topographical Maps

##### Points to Remember

Topographical maps are large-scale maps that show both natural and man-made features.

These are the features of the grid system.

This is how the representation of relief or elevation on a topo sheet is done using contours

The shape of the land is generally shown by contour lines. It is also known as a topo sheet.

The lines that run vertically are called eastings while the lines that run horizontally are called northings.

This is how simple landforms are identified on a topo sheet

Eastings and northings cross each other to form a square known as a grid square.

Using contours is the most common method of showing relief or elevation on topo sheets.

This is how settlement patterns are shown on topo sheets

This is how transport and communication are shown on a topo sheet

Gentle slope and steep slope, plateau, conical hill, ridge, saddle, cliff, waterfall, V-shaped valley, U-shaped valley, col, pass, gap

Types of settlements: Nucleated settlements, lineal settlements, scattered settlements

Metalled roads (trucks, buses, cars etc.); Nor

metalled roads (cart tracks, pack tracks, footpaths

There are three types of railway gauges: broad metre, narrow.

How to read and interpret a topographical map

Sheet number, scale, grid, direction on map sheet, eatsings and northings, four-figure and six-figure grid squares, legend keys, contour interval, spot heights, triangulated stations, con index, depression (dep), confluence, dry and wet streams, et

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//788be9b8-e576-44f2-8046-3654d709a96e/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_204_142_271_197.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A26Z%2F-1%2F%2F0e82361b32333d536934b6678f27b245a12db3033c77d8222486d7a15c9925fe" alt="Image" width="5%" /></div>


#### Important Terms

Contour line: An imaginary line on a map connecting points at the same height above sea level

Eastings: Lines that run vertically across a topographical map, measured eastwards from the south-west corner

Northings: Lines that run horizontally across a topographical map, measured northwards from the south-west corner

Topographical maps: Large-scale maps that show both natural features, such as mountains, hills, rivers, lakes, plateaus, cliffs, and human-made features such as roads, railway tracks, and wells

Vertical Interval (VI): The interval (difference in value) between adjacent contour lines

Horizontal Equivalent (HE): The distance between two adjacent contour lines

Watershed: A highland where streams on one side flow into one river and streams on the other side flow into a different river

Nucleated settlement: A settlement in which the houses are in a compact cluster

Linear settlement: A settlement that develops in a line on either side of a road or a railway track

Scattered settlement: A settlement that is scattered over a large area, i.e., houses and huts are far apart from one another

Pack track: A rough path or road, usually one that has not been built but that has been made by people/ animals walking there

Cutting: A narrow open passage that is dug through high ground for a road, railway or canal

Causeway: A raised road or path across water or wet ground

3. Contour lines do not ___ one another.

5. Houses or huts in ___ settlement are far apart from one another.

D. State whether the following are true or false. Rewrite the false sentences correctly.

1. A contour line is an imaginary line that connects all points having the same temperature.

2. The lines that run vertically are called northings.

3. Contour lines are drawn at fixed intervals.

4. A gap is a low-lying depression or a valley which cuts through a range of hills.

5. A spot height on a map is indicated with a small triangle followed by the number.

# James Rennell and the Map of Hindoostan

James Hennell (1742-1830) was an English geographer, historian and oceanographer.

While serving in the British Royal Navy from 1756 to 1763,

Rennell learned the skills of an expert coloniel surveyor.

He joined the East India Company in 1763.

Robert Clive, the English General who led the British to victory in the Battle of Plassey in 1757 (in which the British captured Bengal), appointed him the Surveyor General of Bengal in 1767. He served in this post till 1777.

It is said that Clive appointed him to make maps for the company set it was easier to control a large territory like India if they knew what it looked like and how much area it occupied.

INDIA K

T18ET

DAY OF

BENGAL

Erich sentur

Present international

boundary of India

Rensell began his survey of Bengal in 1764. He compiled his findings in The Bengal Atlas, published in 1779. Rennell's maps were the most accurate ones for the next 60 years.

The Bengal Atlas became an important asset for the commercial, administrative and military activities of the English East India Company.

He carried out the first comprehensive geographical survey of India. The survey was a massive undertaking that mapped parts of India at a greater detail than many European countries had been mapped.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//9ecc5a8c-adf7-4c2a-b9a0-49bc3bfbfce9/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_3_222_561_744.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F567770d7fe9c259144f75ceed3f8093d617388e1bc607d3ac103dd791789a6ba" alt="Image" width="46%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//9ecc5a8c-adf7-4c2a-b9a0-49bc3bfbfce9/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_568_171_1190_642.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F09dccc95f6b729b94828551f873e7cfd15679b752defccffaf25ae9ca5cb41af" alt="Image" width="52%" /></div>


His cartographic methods included gathering information from earlier maps, measuring distances along roads, establishing the coordinates of control points, and then creating a 'graticule' or grid to create his maps. Rennell's maps were of such accuracy and quality that they were used well into the 19th century.

Rennell created the Map of Hindoston in 1782 after conducting groundbreaking surveys to the Indian subcontinent. He showed the regions in great detail. This map is said to be 'the first approximately correct map of India'.

The boundaries of India at the end of the 18th century are shown in line with the rise of British dominance.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//9ecc5a8c-adf7-4c2a-b9a0-49bc3bfbfce9/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_2_973_431_1616.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2Fcd101c76698fbefcd8d384d956943914abac54fb163170c84c4d5f241b27b1bc" alt="Image" width="36%" /></div>


The cartouche shows Britain as a lion dominating the globe. The pundits are shown offering sacred texts to the female warrior Britannia, representing Britain's Interest in Indian customary laws and practices. Britannia stands on a pedestal which has British victories engraved on it. Ships sail in the background showing British naval power.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//9ecc5a8c-adf7-4c2a-b9a0-49bc3bfbfce9/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_425_791_1174_1606.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F6f28007ed369c531a45509acc5e2d751bfdcdf240cd6819d00f97b8c10917bae" alt="Image" width="62%" /></div>


Red was used as a code for British imperial dominance. Rennell is said to have started this tradition of denoting British imperial territories in red.

##### Skill: Communication

Try to find out about the type of settlement your city/town/village is. Based on the information gathered, prepare a brief write-up on your city.

#### WHAT IS POPULATION?

The term population means the number of inhabitants who live in a particular country or region. The world we live in today has more than 8 billion people and growing by the day. However, the total land area is only 510 million square km, out of which humans occupy around 64 million square km. These are the continental masses, namely North America, South America, Europe, Asia, the Oceanic countries consisting of Australia, New Zealand and the South Pacific Islands of Melanesia, Micronesia and Polynesia.

Biodiversity loss, climate change, pollution, deforestation, water and food shortages have all been exacerbated (made worse) by the huge and our ever-increasing numbers leading to ever-increasing consumption. While the human population between the period 1970–2016 increased by more than 103

per cent, wild vertebrate animal population like elephants, tigers, orangutans, wolves, leopards, foxes, polar bears and so de-

United Nations estimates, global population continues to grow by around 1 per cent 80 million people every year. Countries have the highest population in 2023 are India and China, surpassing a billion people each USA, Indonesia, Pakistan, Nigeria, Brazil, Bangladesh, Russia and Mexico also have very large populations.

#### DISTRIBUTION OF POPULATION

Continent-wise, Asia has the large population, with over 4.7 billion people followed by Africa with 1.46 billion people in Europe has over 741 million people, No America has over 604 million people in South America has over 439 million people and Oceania (Australia, New Zealand and the Pacific Islands of Fiji, Papua Guinea, Vanuatu, Samoa, etc.) has over 7 million people.

According to a report by the United Nations Population Fund published in April 2009, the world's largest countries, India has the largest population.

population in the world, with over 1.28 billion people and China coming second with over 1.425 billion people. On the other hand, Canada has only about 38.7 million people with a vast land area of 10 million square km and a population density of 4 persons per square km. The current world population is more than 8 billion. This is frightening for humans and for the planet as a whole.

##### IMPORTANT FEATURES OF POPULATION

To better understand the population of a country, we need to learn some important terms given below:

Birth rate is number of live births per year per 1,000 of the population. The formula for calculating birth rate is:

 $$ \frac{Number of births}{Total population}\times1,000 $$ 

Death rate is number of deaths per year per 1,000 of the population. The formula for calculating death rate is:

 $$ \mathrm{\frac{Number~of~deaths}{Total population}}\times1,000 $$ 

Life expectancy is the number of years that a person is likely to live.

Population density refers to the number of people living in a unit area of space, such as a square kilometre.

## FACTORS AFFECTING THE POPULATION OF A PLACE

Various factors affect the population of a place. Let us discuss some of these in the following pages.

#### Birth Rate and Death Rate

The high birth rate in a country leads to an increase in population and a high death rate causes a decrease in population. There was an increase in human population in Europe and North America during the Industrial Revolution in the 18th century. It was not only because the birth rate increased but also because the death rate started to fall. Death rates declined as new developments in agricultural practices and transportation technology increased the food supply and reduced the danger of famine. Public health and living standards had improved due to new technologies and industrial development.

In some countries, declining birth rates and an increase in death rates have led to a decline in population size.

Over the last several decades, the death rate in India has declined and life expectancy has improved. Moreover, several factors are responsible for improvement of life expectancy in the country. These are:

1. Improvement in healthcare and hygiene

2. Improvement in sanitary conditions, particularly in rural areas (Schemes like Swacchh Bharat)

3. Improvement in education standards with more schools being built.

4. Improvement in Mid-Day Meal Scheme for schoolchildren who are provided more nutritious diet.

5. Improvement in medical care with more healthcare centres and free vaccinations for diseases such as cholera, tuberculosis, Covid-19 ctc, leading to better control of epidemics.

6. Better flood control and famine management.

7. Better management of natural disasters

### Immigration and Emigration

The population of a place is greatly impacted by factors like immigration and emigration. The process of coming to live permanently in another country that is not one's own is called immigration (into a country). The process of leaving one's own country to go and live permanently in another country is called emigration (where people exit a country). When people immigrate to a country, the population of that country increases. The population of a place declines when people emigrate from a country.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//9ecc5a8c-adf7-4c2a-b9a0-49bc3bfbfce9/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_721_84_1190_468.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F8e31309a898d2fdbb4fb7d3cce1b320bb3f6fae1fcf3a3e0f86aae5eab957bf5" alt="Image" width="39%" /></div>

Discuss whether improved and advanced medical technology and better healthcare facilities are both a boon and a bane for India. You can give reasons to support your point of view.

#### Influx of Refugees

Refugees from different countries at different times also increase the population of country. India has always opened its border to all people who come looking for safe and shelter. There are people from Tibetan, Afghanistan, Bangladesh and Myanmar living in India and it has maintained an open door policy for all. As a result, the population of India has sharply increased.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//9ecc5a8c-adf7-4c2a-b9a0-49bc3bfbfce9/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_683_1197_1190_1600.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F4edc0ec880f8dcd5667fde849986d15cbc777775cc8c06104b3caa3116a9346c" alt="Image" width="42%" /></div>


A ret.

#### (Urbanization)

Migration from rural areas to urban areas has been a continuous process. It happened earlier in developed countries and is happening today in developing countries as well. Migration has a significant impact on population growth. When a country is highly urbanized, the birth rate tends to rise and death rates tend to fall. There is an increase in the birth rates as people have more access to medical care in cities than in rural areas, and hence, infant mortality falls and the birth rate rises. However, in urban areas, birth rates also decline as the government launches awareness campaigns and sets up family planning programmes to help people plan small families. Death rates decline in urban areas because of better medical and education services, and more reliable food supplies. This is often not the case in remote rural areas, so death rates fall in urban areas. As a result, there is population growth due to urbanization.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e02032be-f09d-405b-9718-6ca7ef67173d/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_18_846_581_1195.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2Fc437abb0db881f890bb524e0f1462c24bc481d78a7be112e8cac2133bbcd8eb7" alt="Image" width="47%" /></div>


▲ Migration has a significant impact on population growth.

##### Agricultural Development

Changes and developments in agricultural methods have led to increased agricultural production. The mechanization of agriculture has freed up workers from the farms. It has encouraged industrialization which needs lots of workers. It tends to promote high birth

rates. Moreover, the increased agricultural production has reduced the deaths due to famine, thereby causing the population to grow.
