##### HOTS Question

##### SKIN: AnalysISIE

Singapore has a very high population density. However, it also has high standards of living and provides sufficient resources for its people. Why do you think the negative effects of overpopulation are not so pronounced in Singapore?

##### Education

Education plays an important role in determining the level of population growth in a country. Simple programmes in hygiene can reduce death rates, while family planning programmes can reduce birth rates. The governments in various countries have launched massive awareness campaigns on population growth and help people to plan families. Eventually, the educational and awareness levels of people also have an impact on the growth of the population.

##### Topography and Climate of a Place

Population also grows in areas where the land is flat and is cultivable and water is available in plenty for both agricultural and domestic purposes. The cities that grow on the banks of rivers have a large population. The climate of a place is also an important

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e02032be-f09d-405b-9718-6ca7ef67173d/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_263_33_1108_710.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F250a42acec4c204abedb2389bc19c284b237aac7f62731a424e2f5c54f25c509" alt="Image" width="71%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">▲ World: population density</div> </div>


factor in determining the population growth. If the climate is pleasant, it will attract population. Climate, relief features, soil quality and proximity to natural resources have influenced human life.

##### Transport and Communication

Population of a place grows if it is easily accessible by various kinds of roads, rivers and railway lines. Communication systems like internet, phone and post is essential in today's living and so places with these facilities have more population.

##### Employment Opportunities

Population of a place grows if there are prospects for employment. Mines and industries in the area are potential sources of employment and therefore, encourage population growth.

#### OVERPOPULATION

Overpopulation is a very undesirable condition where the number of people in a particular area exceeds the availability resources to meet the needs of all the people in the area. In an overpopulated environment the number of people might be more than the available essential materials for surviving such as food, clothes, water, shelter, transport and other amenities.

Overpopulation is caused by a number factors such as immigration, increased birth rates and decreased death rates, better medical facilities and lack of family planning.

In the developed countries of the world, the population increased earlier due to:

economic growth and prosperity as a result of industrialization.

· improved medical techniques and healthcare facilities.

immigration because of better opportunities and better living conditions

In developing countries of the world, rapid increase in population was due to:

- modern medical techniques which increased the lifespan of the people.

ignorance of the masses.

- traditional beliefs, customs and outlooks of people.

##### IMPACT OF OVERPOPULATION

Overpopulation usually has an adverse effect on the environment, the economy and the quality of life that people lead.

- A larger population consumes more natural resources such as fresh water, arable land and mineral resources.

- As more land is brought under cultivation, the amount of land under forests keeps reducing, impacting the diverse animal and plant populations in these forests.

• Increased mining for minerals causes further environmental damage.

- As more factories are set up to meet the needs of the people, more fossil fuels are used and more pollutants are released into the environment.

In developed countries, the death rates have reduced and the lifespan of the people have increased due to improvements in medical facilities. As a result, the number of elderly people has also increased tremendously. This has increased the financial burden on the governments as they now have to support and pay pensions to a large number of people.

In developing countries, the growing population has led to significant problems as there are many people competing for scarce resources and the basic necessities of life have become expensive. There is not enough affordable food, shelter and education for everyone. Large parts of the population live in small, congested areas with poor sanitary conditions. This leads to the rapid spread of diseases, which puts a strain on the medical

services that are available. There are not enough jobs, so people are unable to break free from the cycle of poverty. In such conditions, there is ample scope for a rise in crime and conflict.

Countries like India have become overcrowded because of the following reasons:

As there is not enough land for everyone in the villages, people have been forced to settle in towns and cities.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e02032be-f09d-405b-9718-6ca7ef67173d/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_595_392_1156_807.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2F2f0ac8c2121b2559545840c8df47dd5e54fcc63a0a50c3003194fc05b3341a7c" alt="Image" width="47%" /></div>


Overpopulation puts immense pressure on the resources.

However, even in these towns and cities, there is an acute shortage of houses and jobs. Homeless, unemployed and poverty-stricken people are forced to live on the streets. As a result in some cities, slums have mushroomed where the living conditions are very poor.

There are problems of water supply, lighting, sanitation, drainage and hygiene in the slums.

As the lives of the pavement and slum dwellers are miserable, it has led to serious social and economic problems, such as hunger, starvation, malnutrition, disease poor health, illiteracy, and ignorance.

- Crime rate and corruption have an increased manifold.

Overpopulation has serious consequences on the planet. Humans have already consumed 35 per cent of the planet's existing resources including food, water, forests, soil, and so on. Because of the huge demand for food, and minerals, agricultural land has gradually expanded at the cost of forests, meadows, pastures and rivers. As more arable land is brought under cultivation, forests keep reducing. This impacts the habitats of wild animals and rare and useful herbs and plants. Moreover, the increase in manufacturing industries has a tremendous negative impact on the environment, soil, air, water and the biodiversity in general, leading to environmental degradation. According to an American ecologist, geographer and biologist named Prof. Jared, humanity has just one generation, that is, your generation, to save the planet from collapse and just to remind us there is no Planet B.

- Fast deforestation and deforestation at this rate means there will be no rainforests left by the time you are 60 years old!

- 0.01% of humanity has caused the extinction of 83 per cent of all wildlife and 60 per cent of all plants!

Humans have manufactured and consumed so much plastic that during the last 70 years the earth is almost plastic-coated.

Overpopulation hampers the pace of economic progress and development in developing countries. This is because the wealth that would have been used for industrial growth and development is being used by the government to provide food, shelter and basic education to the growing population in these countries. Similarly, healthcare facilities are unable to cope with the ever-increasing population, leading to a breakdown of healthcare services, and as such, several diseases are common in the slums.

#### Knowledge of India

The Registrar General and Census Commission of India (Ministry of Home Affairs, Government of India) holds a pivotal role in the nation's governance. This government authority is entrusted with the monumental task of conducting the decennial census, providing crucial insights into India's population, demographics, and socio-economic characteristics. Beyond the census, it also maintains vital statistics, supporting research and informed policymaking. This office ensures that data on births and deaths, housing and linguistics are also collected and analyzed, contributing significantly to India's resource allocation and planning efforts. Its work underscores the importance of data-driven decision-making in a country as diverse and dynamic as India.

Many countries, including India, became self-sufficient in food supplies during the Green Revolution in agriculture in the 1960s and 1970s. However, the population explosion negated the Green Revolution in the 1980s as the number of additional mouths to feed also increased rapidly. Industrial development, urbanization and soil erosion have reduced the amount of available agricultural land. As a consequence, food production could not increase to meet the needs of the increased population.

##### UNDERPOPULATION

Underpopulation occurs when the size of the population of a place is small in relation to the available resources of a country. This happens when there are not enough people to make full use of resources such as land, water and forests and the available technology. Underpopulation may be caused by an increase in death rates caused mainly by

natural disasters like earthquakes, tsunamis, floods or manmade disasters such as war. The effect of these calamities are felt all the more in a country whose population is not large. Another cause is due to epidemics such as cholera, Covid-19, malaria, typhoid, etc.

Underpopulation can also occur because of a reduction in birth rates (countries like Italy, Spain, Romania and the Scandinavian countries like Norway, Sweden, Finland and Denmark and Iceland) or due to genetic reasons or higher rates of infertility in the general populace (Countries like South Korea and Japan). High rates of emigration (people moving out of a country) can also lead to underpopulation.

##### Impact of Underpopulation

There are several positive impacts of underpopulation.

1. There are sufficient employment opportunities for everyone.

2. 'There are fewer instances of overcrowding.

3. Poverty is either non-existent or low.

4. There are adequate schools, medical facilities, and specialty hospitals to meet the needs of everyone.

5. There are sufficient natural resources to meet the requirements of the population.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e02032be-f09d-405b-9718-6ca7ef67173d/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_41_1102_557_1433.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F63baa080eaf3519a5fb8eb236fc462cbfaaf84b6f01a34a5e7e62aeff68e0064" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>


Underpopulation puts less pressure on the environment.

6. Above all, there is less pressure on the environment and biodiversity, hence lower environmental degradation.

7. The overall traffic flow is less and as a result, the Air Quality Index (AQI) of every town is good with less pollution related ailments.

However, there are some negative impacts as well.

1. Lack of people for jobs. This leads to low production.

2. In some cases, a high proportion of the population is either too old or too young to work.

3. There are fewer taxpayers which means less money for the government.

4. There are not enough people to develop the natural resources of the country.

5. Most areas of the country remain uninhabited, leading to great difficulty in exploring more natural resources.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e02032be-f09d-405b-9718-6ca7ef67173d/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_575_840_1097_948.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F715a78dd4a4a759d604467c57536f26c1f69cd33b62c6f81dacf169413d2bafd" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>


In what ways can underpopulation affect the long-term sustainability and progress of a country? C-6.3

##### COMPOSITION OF POPULATION

Population composition or demographic structure refers to the physical, socio-cultural and economic attributes of the population such as age and sex, place of residence, language, religion, marital status, literacy, etc. These are the characteristics of the population which are measurable and help in distinguishing one group from another. Let us read about two of these characteristics.

##### Rural and Urban Composition

The population of a country may be classified into rural and urban on the basis of where a person resides. The rural population refers to the people residing in villages, while the urban population refers to the people living in towns and cities. In India, for instance, 69 per cent of the population resides in villages and 31 per cent resides in towns and cities.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fa23f740-7312-4874-9dc6-6a760340fd39/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_120_439_649_783.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A26Z%2F-1%2F%2F9e6d5dcdb5c839f2ae1fc7c2c46f1ed98064b93e0d19804d9bd62f5e8e4166a9" alt="Image" width="44%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">Most Indians live in villages.</div> </div>


This division is necessary because rural and urban populations differ from each other in various aspects—population density, occupations and livelihood, presence of various amenities, transport and communication facilities and the socio-cultural environment.

Rural areas generally have a lower population density. The people living in villages are typically engaged in primary activities such as farming, fishing, mining, etc. The educational and medical facilities are usually not very highly developed. Opportunities for higher education are fewer. Transport and communication facilities are not of a very high standard. Village communities are usually closely knit, with a strong emphasis on culture and traditions.

Urban areas generally have a higher population density. People living in these areas are usually engaged in secondary and tertiary activities such as trade, transport, services, etc. There are better facilities for education, healthcare, and communication. There is also more opportunity for economic growth. However, the socio-cultural ties between people's cities are not as strong as those in villages, recent years, the urban population has rise and the rural population has declined as much as more people from villages have moved.

Age composition refers to the percentage of people in different age groups in a given population. It differs from country to country. The section of the population between 14 to 60 years of age is considered to be the working population. A higher working population is considered an asset for a country as it means that there is a high availability of labour for the development of the nation. India has one of the highest percentages of population in the younger age group. According to the 201 Census, 30.7 per cent of the population is the country is in the age group of 0-14 years around 61.3 per cent in the age group 15 to 50 and, 8 per cent of the population is in the age group 60 and above.

##### Age and Sex Composition

Another characteristic that helps us to study the population is called the sex ratio. It reflects the comparative numbers of males and females in the population. In India, the sex ratio is calculated in terms of females per 1,000 males. The formula to calculate the sex ratio is:

 $ \frac{\text{Female population}}{\text{Male population}} \times 1000 $

For instance, when we say that the sex ratio in India is 943, it means that there are 94 girls for every 1,000 boys. The sex ratio is

considered favourable if there is an equal or a higher number of females per 1,000 males in the population. An adverse or unfavourable sex ratio means that there is a lower number of females per 1,000 males in the population.

The sex ratio is usually unfavourable in those countries where gender discrimination is widespread and women are considered to have a lower status in society. Practices of female foeticide (killing of girls in the womb), female infanticide (killing of girls when they are babies) and domestic violence towards women can lead to an unfavourable sex ratio.

The average sex ratio in the world is 984 females to every 1,000 males. Countries like India, Pakistan, China, Saudi Arabia and Afghanistan have lower-than-average sex ratios. Qatar, a country in Asia, has the lowest sex ratio in the world, with 334 females per 1,000 males. On the other hand, countries in Europe have a higher-than-average sex ratio. Latvia in Europe has the highest sex ratio, with 1,173 females for every 1,000 males.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fa23f740-7312-4874-9dc6-6a760340fd39/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_22_867_84_937.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A26Z%2F-1%2F%2Ff8bc7bc4a1ea939801b8aceb0924a62fb90da113964b868e6cd822f70faf68ff" alt="Image" width="5%" /></div>


##### Quick Facts

According to the 2011 Census of India, the state of Haryana in India had the worst sex ratio with only 879 females to every 1,000 males. Female foeticide and infanticide are still rampant across India, despite strict bans on determination of the sex of a child during pregnancy.

### POPULATION PYRAMID OR AGE SEX PYRAMID

A population pyramid is a specially designed diagram that shows the age and sex composition of a population. It is called a population pyramid because the diagram resembles a pyramid. It is perhaps the most effective way to show the age and sex structure of a population.

##### Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs)

(Goal-8: Decent Work and Economic Growth)

The goal is to promote inclusive and sustainable economic growth, regular employment and decent work environment for all. In India, the government has started various schemes to ensure that people, especially the youth, have sustainable work opportunities through programmes such as Make in India, Startup India, Skill India and Digital India. Read newspapers, magazines and search the internet to gather information on these programmes.

The diagram consists of bars arranged in the form of a pyramid, with the longer bars at the base and the shorter ones at the top. The bars show different age groups, with the males on the left and the females on the right. The base represents the youngest age group and the apex represents the oldest. The age groups are arranged in an ascending order vertically, with the youngest age group at the bottom. The shape of the population pyramid shows the characteristics of the population. We shall study three types of pyramids briefly.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fa23f740-7312-4874-9dc6-6a760340fd39/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_582_914_678_988.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A26Z%2F-1%2F%2F0e0336d3df55accb6f5573f11d789ce655a7bd0348e5cd2c3faff0bdc490665c" alt="Image" width="8%" /></div>


#### Did You Know?

Beti Bachao, Beti Padhao (Save the girl child, educate the girl child) is a scheme launched by the government of India that works towards generating awareness and improving the efficiency of welfare services meant for women in the country.

##### Expanding Population

In this case, the age-sex pyramid is more or less triangular, with a broad base and a narrow apex. The broad base shows a larger proportion of the population in the lower age group, which is an indication of a high birth rate. The narrow apex on top shows the high death rate in the older age group. Such a

pyramid indicates rapid population growth. Countries like Nigeria, Bangladesh, India and Mexico will have such a population pyramid.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fa23f740-7312-4874-9dc6-6a760340fd39/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_chart_box_175_201_575_720.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2F415dc8b44affc41cb922981b532c45862dc3f42e4ba25d71dee29810b982c005" alt="Image" width="33%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">▲ Expanding population</div> </div>


##### Constant Population

Here, the pyramid is almost shaped like a bell, with a narrow top and a broad middle for several bars.

It shows that the birth rate is almost equal to the death rate, leading to a constant population with the percentage of males and females remaining almost the same. Usually developed countries such as the USA have this kind of a pyramid.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fa23f740-7312-4874-9dc6-6a760340fd39/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_chart_box_188_958_574_1492.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2F660803ffad9e646cc6134ad9a276bc3b93215ca60c88d3f630d287b541e0d998" alt="Image" width="32%" /></div>


Constant population

#### Declining Population

The pyramid depicting a declining population has a narrow base, a bulging middle that reflects low birth and death rates and a slightly narrow apex. Countries like Japan, Germany and Italy have this kind of pyramid.

Studying the population helps us understand how it shapes the world in different ways. Harnessing the population correctly is an important task for the government. It plays a big role in the development of a country.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fa23f740-7312-4874-9dc6-6a760340fd39/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_chart_box_682_728_1160_1392.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2F9a31975666cf9139b3d8b151836dcbfe79a369a6465365947a7caf222c15bc22" alt="Image" width="40%" /></div>


Declining population

##### Values and Life Skills

A high population is not of much value to a nation if the people are not well-educated or trained. The government and people of a country should strive to ensure that education reaches as many people in the country as possible.

How can you help in the task of educating people around you who have not had the chance to go to school?

##### Biography

Thomas Robert Malthus (1766–1834 CE) was an English economist and demographer. He is best known for his Population Theory in which he stated that populations inevitably expand until they outgrow their available food supply, in return causing the population growth to be reversed by famine, disease, war or calamity. He also developed an exponential formula to get a forecast of population growth, known as the Malthusian growth model.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fa23f740-7312-4874-9dc6-6a760340fd39/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_881_441_1081_634.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F09752b5efeb08340259388615624f9e50fe94f4ccb682265253a01d4f23dcec2" alt="Image" width="16%" /></div>


##### Points to Remember

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fa23f740-7312-4874-9dc6-6a760340fd39/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_36_679_1109_1559.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2Fa330348e64ee8ca797dc0fa88a64f370d0595cf7d5604b939cf4eeb73c4fdbed" alt="Image" width="90%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fa23f740-7312-4874-9dc6-6a760340fd39/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_203_19_270_83.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F4162d938c7f1cff7e30b667bff3ec127dd0c018b5d9c07b40d321de43cfd6cad" alt="Image" width="5%" /></div>


##### Important Terms

Birth rate: The number of births every year for every 1,000 of the population

Population: All the people who live in a particular area, city or country

Death rate: The number of deaths every year for every 1,000 of the population

Life expectancy: The number of years that a person is likely to live

Population density: The number of people living in a unit area of space, such as a square kilometre

Immigration: The process of coming to live permanently in another country that is not one's own

Emigration: The process of leaving one country to go and live permanently in another country

Refugee: A refugee is a person who has been forced to leave their country in order to escape war, persecution, or natural disaster

Family planning: The process of controlling the number of children that a person has

Infertility: Not being able to have babies or produce young ones

Demographic: Related to the population and different groups within it

Sex ratio: The number of females per 1,000 males in the population

### 1. Source-based questions

Read the following passage and answer the questions.

Cross-border migration refers to the movement of individuals from one country to another. It has an impact on the populations of both the countries. Emigration means leaving one's own country to settle in another country. It is a result of a variety of circumstances, including war, education, search for new jobs, or opportunity to reunite with one's family. When a person leaves a country, the population of that country decreases. Immigration occurs when a person arrives in a country from another country. The country that hosts this person decides if it will allow the person to immigrate or not. The change in the number of people during a certain time period is referred to as population change. This change occurs as a result of births, deaths, and movement of individuals. The difference between a country's birth and mortality rates is known as its natural growth rate.

##### Recall

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//363fb6f5-8695-41ac-a1b8-21964d8bd453/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_255_706_328_770.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2Ff376d75ea3745527ef17a61a79ebe6c072f54d21bb5853f47482f2c9da4e8922" alt="Image" width="6%" /></div>


##### Skill: Communication

You learnt about immigration and emigration in the last lesson. Discuss how these terms are related to migration.

Migration refers to the movement of people from one place to another. There may be many types of migration, including international and intra-national. International migration takes place when people move from one country to another. Intra-national migration takes place within a country from one state or region, district, city or town to another state, region, district, city or town.

Migration is normal human behavior and a global phenomenon. Our ancestors in the prehistoric era were hunters-gatherers. They were constantly on the move in search of food and shelter. Floods, storms and earthquakes too compelled them to move from one place to another. Agriculture began and man started to settle in one place.

Migration is classified into many types and for various reasons. A person who shifts from one country, city or town or village to another country city, town or village is called a migrant. The person can also be someone who crosses international borders to escape religious or political persecution. Under normal circumstances, a migrant can be a person who moves to another country for better job opportunities and education prospects.

##### TYPES OF MIGRATION

Following is a list of broad types of migration:

- Migration can be internal—people moving within the country from one place to another. It can also be external—people moving to a new country or continent.

When a person leaves his or her own country and moves to another, it is called emigration. The person who emigrates is known as an emigrant from his or her own country. For example, when a person leaves India and goes to Canada to settle there, that person is said to have emigrated from India to Canada.

When a person arrives in a new country after leaving his or her own country, it is called immigration. For example, a person who arrives in Canada from India is said to have immigrated to Canada and is known as an immigrant in Canada.

- Temporary migration could be annual, seasonal or daily. For example, people may move to lower regions from mountains during harsh winter months.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//363fb6f5-8695-41ac-a1b8-21964d8bd453/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_125_443_641_830.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F7b0d347f0e7f6e3e974da74bd04b9eeb25a32851b4c2cd938f269804d9093490" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>


Immigrant farm workers in southern Greece

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//363fb6f5-8695-41ac-a1b8-21964d8bd453/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_134_895_220_968.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F76a2b8a17bfda293af5f5ff4378f85642f654cd357cf82290799006b57904c7a" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>


##### Did You Know?

Early human migration is believed to have started when Homo Erectus first migrated out of Africa to Eurasia about 1.8 million years ago.

### Migration between Rural and Urban Areas

Based on the direction of movement, migration is of four types. These are:

1. rural to urban 2. rural to rural 3. urban to urban 4. urban to rural

##### Rural to urban migration

In this type of migration, people move from rural areas (villages) to cities in search of better employment opportunities. In villages there are little or no jobs. So, the only way a person could earn their living is to go to the city (urban) area either alone or with their family. Moreover, in urban areas there are better educational opportunities and the opportunity to adapt to and enjoy an urban lifestyle and health services. This type of migration is common in developing countries like India, Brazil and Sri Lanka. Apart from this, other reasons are:

- a village cannot support a rapid increase in population.

• food supply is limited.

- land on which to cultivate or build house is scarce.

• introduction of mechanized farming where machines replace labour.

marriage, which is one of the biggest causes of migration.

quality of housing and cost of living.

• education.

##### Rural to rural migration

This type of migration takes place when people move from one rural area to another. This happens for various reasons—acquisition of property, marriage, better resources, etc. In rural India, girls usually leave their villages after marriage and go to live with their husbands in their villages.

Many people also leave their own villages and migrate to different villages where they buy land because it is more fertile.

##### Urban to urban migration

Migration from one city to another happens when people of one city choose to go to another city, generally a larger one, in search of better jobs, educational facilities, health facilities, etc. For example, many students and professionals from cities like Patna, Prayagraj and Lucknow go to Delhi in search of better opportunities. This type of

migration also happens when the population of a city becomes too big and begins to affect the quality of life there. As a result, many people choose to shift to a new city where the quality of life is satisfactory. For example, people from Delhi are moving to satellite towns like Gurugram and Noida because these cities also have satisfactory amenities.

Moving a large government office or other establishments from one city to another also causes large-scale migration of people from one city to another.

##### Urban to rural migration

In this type of migration, people go back to their homes in the village for several reasons such as to look after the property left behind by their parents or to marry from there. Some people also return when they find there are no suitable job opportunities in the city, or are unable to find proper shelter. Sometimes, the cost of living in the city is very high or the migrants are unable to cope with the traffic and pollution. Urban-rural migration is common in countries like Pakistan and Afghanistan.

##### Other Forms of Migration

Beside the types of migration mentioned, there are other forms of migration as well, such as primitive migration, forced migration, free migration and illegal migration.

##### Primitive migration

Primitive migration is one in which people respond to an unfavourable environment by leaving it for a more favourable one. Pre-industrial societies tend to make such decisions on a group basis rather than on an individual basis. The hunting and gathering groups (which still exist in many parts of the world) might migrate regularly as the resources of the area get depleted. Some farming communities might move as the soil becomes infertile. Primitive migration also occurs when additional land is needed as populations increase in size.

##### Forced migration

When people living in a place are forced to leave the place due to reasons like poor living conditions, persecution, lack of political freedom, wars, lack of means to earn a

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//363fb6f5-8695-41ac-a1b8-21964d8bd453/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_14_1008_1080_1485.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F6014b62f25eae729e57ebdfe371c1926c26fc57e45cbc53af7cd75a1c59e8605" alt="Image" width="89%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">World Migration</div> </div>


livelihood, famine, etc., then it is called forced migration. Forced migration is involuntary.

##### Free migration

Illegal migration is one where people violate immigration laws and move to other countries. It is the crossing of a country's border by a person or group of persons by violating the immigration laws of the destination country. In such cases, migration becomes illegal.

In free migration, people have the choice to either stay or move. The decision to move is based on people's personal choice and it is mostly guided by factors like better job opportunities and better living conditions. These people often analyse the advantages and disadvantages of moving to a new place and then make an informed decision.

##### Illegal migration

##### WHY PEOPLE MIGRATE?

There are many reasons why people migrate to other places. Some reasons are economic and some are political. But underlying these population movements is the desire for change and the idea of a new life that sets them to a new environment. In many cases of migration, there are various factors which induce people to move. The rural-urban migration in developing countries is influenced not only by the pull or attraction of the cities and towns, but also because of low incomes, difficult living conditions and lack of source of livelihood in rural areas, which push people into leaving their homes.

##### Push Factors

Sometimes, people have a choice to migrate according to their wish, but sometimes they are forced to migrate. The reason people are forced to leave a place is called the push

factor. Some of the push factors are:

Lack of jobs in their own country or state

War is one factor. In the face of an ongoing violent war in Syria, thousands of Syrians have made difficult journeys to migrate to safer countries, just across the Syrian borders or even further.

Food and essentials become scarce and expensive due to famine or political instability. The severe food scarcity in Venezuela in 2016 forced many Venezuelans to flock to neighbouring countries such as Columbia in search of food and medicines. The economic crisis in Greece in 2015 led to severe shortages of food and medicine, forcing people to migrate. The severe shortage of food grains in Nigeria in 2016 resulted in many Nigerians trying to cross over into neighbouring countries.

Natural disasters are also a factor. The 2015 earthquake in Nepal caused many people to migrate to India.

• Poverty

• Increased crime rates

• Extreme weather conditions

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//98790e48-ae4d-4427-bd6d-70bd421ac0c7/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_668_1019_1173_1354.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A25Z%2F-1%2F%2F35cee82dbe4003ca264b7fc639defd2f621eadcadea661702d58cec04668ff3b" alt="Image" width="42%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">▲ A refugee camp with tents</div> </div>


##### Lack of job opportunities

People living in villages often move to cities and towns in search of better job

Bihar, Jharkhand and West Bengal move to Punjab, Haryana and Delhi in search of better job opportunities in these states where they get employment on agricultural lands, construction sites and factories. Some of them also work as domestic help in urban households. In this way, they earn better incomes and also improve their living conditions. Unemployed city dwellers may also move to other towns or cities within their own country or overseas in order to get jobs. People move to other countries also because the salaries and wages may be less compared to the countries where they migrate, for example, lots of Indians and Pakistanis have moved to the UK, Canada, and other industrialized countries of the world to earn higher wages.

##### Lack of available land

Sometimes, farmers cannot make a living in their own country because there is a shortage of land, or the quality of land is too poor. In such cases, such people move to places where land is available. This was the main motive of many migrations in the past. History tells us that the USA, Australia and South Africa were populated by Europeans who were either landless peasants in search of farmlands or farmers who were looking for larger plots of land instead of small plots.

##### Religion

Sometimes, when people of a particular religion are persecuted or when sects are not tolerated, then in order to escape repression, people move to places where they are allowed to practise their religion without any danger of being repressed. The movement of Jews to Israel and the huge migration of people between India and Pakistan during Partition in 1948, are some examples.

##### Politics

People sometimes move because they are not happy with the form of government in their own country. Wars also force people to migrate. People may leave a country to avoid subjection to a new regime, to avoid a war, or because they have lost their homes and farms in the war.

##### Pull Factors

The reason why people are attracted to a new place is known as the pull factor. Pull factors include:

Job opportunities in the new country (many migrate to Canada and Australia for this reason)

• Education (many students leave India to study abroad)

• Availability of better medical facilities.

##### Job opportunities

Many people move to other cities within the country or to other countries because of better job and career prospects. These people are also attracted by higher salaries and better quality of life. We have seen recently lots of Indian IT professionals migrating to the USA for better career progression and higher incomes.

##### Education

Many people leave their own country because of educational reasons. They find superior career prospects and increased income because of studying abroad. Many students from India and other Asian countries migrate to the USA, the UK and Australia for further studies in the areas of medicine, engineering and management studies. Some people also migrate from one town to another within the same country because they find better schools and educational institutes there.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//98790e48-ae4d-4427-bd6d-70bd421ac0c7/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_162_63_669_685.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A26Z%2F-1%2F%2Ff1e275737506796f485a19eef2fe2c8ea585e850421d58c3e7db002538d0e7db" alt="Image" width="42%" /></div>


Harvard University in the USA is a popular destination for higher education among the youth.

##### Medical care

People migrate to other places because of better medical care and superior medical facilities. Cities with bigger hospitals, well-known doctors and medical experts, and technically advanced medical systems attract people to move here.

##### Attraction of wealth

Sometimes, the main motive of migration is to earn quick wealth. Discoveries of minerals, especially gold and oil have drawn people from all over the world. Central Australia, Central and South America and South Africa gained population partly because of their gold mines.

##### Climate

Sometimes, people also migrate because of the harsh climate of a place. They prefer to live and settle in places which have pleasant and attractive climate and weather.

##### Family connections

Some migration decisions are influenced by family. People also like to settle in places where they find their own family members gives them a sense of security.

#### Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs)

##### Goal 16: Peace, Justice and Strong Institu

The United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees (UNHCR), the UN Refugee Agency, is an organization which works globally to save lives, protect and build a better future for refugees. It was established in 1950 after the end of World War II in order to help millions who had lost their homes. UNHCR works in 13 countries and provides life-saving assistance, medical attention, food, clean water and shelter to refugees, thus helping them build their lives again.

##### IMPACT OF MIGRATION

Migration can affect both the destinatio country and the home country of the migrati people in both positive and negative ways.

##### Positive Impacts of Migration

Some of the positive socio-economic impact on the destination country are:

Cheap labour: Many migrants are willing to happily take up unskilled jobs for lower wage than is acceptable to the local people. Many Indians, for example, will in countries like UAE and Saudi Arabia lower wages.

Technical and skilled labour: On the other hand, many migrants are high skilled and talented in fields such as computer technology, medicine, teaching space data, etc. The Silicon Valley in US has more Indian and Chinese scientists and technicians than Americans.

Cultural diversity: Immigrants bring their own rich and diverse culture and tradition

when they arrive in a new country. Often, the sharing of cultures, traditions and knowledge helps remove racism and discrimination. German migrants to Canada have introduced their cuisine (food) and religion (Protestantism) to Canada.

When many people leave the country to work abroad, the scope for employment increases for those left behind.

Migration has some positive impacts on the home country as well.

When migrants return home, they bring back knowledge, skills and new ideas. With these, they start their own businesses, thereby providing job opportunities to the local people. In Kerala, migrants returning home after having worked in countries such as UAE and Saudi Arabia, have begun their own businesses such as restaurants, schools, shopping malls, etc.

Migrants working abroad send money home to support their families. This money is called remittance, which indirectly helps the government of the home country too.

##### Negative Impacts of Migration

Migration also has some serious negative impacts on the migrants as well as their destination countries.

Job loss: Many migrants entering a new country rob the job opportunities of the locals because they (the migrants) are willing to work for a lower pay. Many people in the US harbour a sense of resentment towards migrants from Southeast Asia, South Asia, Central and Latin America because they believe the migrants have taken over their jobs.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//98790e48-ae4d-4427-bd6d-70bd421ac0c7/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_537_97_602_167.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2Fe59fa958d9c2d699ff0674abdc2966fe981b585aa562b6ad6e042732c242253a" alt="Image" width="5%" /></div>


Social and civic pressures develop as migrants entering the new country put

##### Quick Facts

1. India saw the sharpest increase in people migrating overseas. According to a report of the United Nations in January 2021, about 10 million (one crore) people left the country between 2000 and 2020.

2. In a report presented in Lok Sabha in 2021, the Government informed the House that 8,81,254 Indians gave up their citizenship from 2015 to September 2021.

3. India has the largest transnational population (Indian people living in foreign countries), with approximately 35 lakh people living in the UAE, 27 lakh in the US, and 25 lakh in Saudi Arabia.

pressure on the existing infrastructure and health and educational facilities meant for the local people. The prices of such amenities shoot up, causing hardship to all.

Immigration can fuel racism and discrimination. Immigrants are often considered different because they speak a different language, dress differently, worship in another way or have a different sets of customs. This sense of difference leads to discrimination and the local people oppose accepting the migrants as a part of the general community.

- Local traditions and cultures are greatly affected because of the introduction of new or alien cultures, traditions and forms of worship. Many people from West Asia and South Asia feel discriminated against in the West because of their dressing habits and religious practices.

Following are the negative impacts of migration on the migrants' home country:

Loss of skilled labour: This is a major disadvantage as young people who have the skill, knowledge and professional expertise

leave their country to offer their services to another country.

Business flourishes when the markets are bigger and have more buyers. A growing and healthy population often provides the required market with economic growth and development. But when young people leave, the population stalls and the demand for some goods and services falls.

A major socio-economic impact of migration is the toll this takes on family life. Young parents leave their children and other dependents, such as the elderly, behind. As a result, the children and the elders who are left behind often have deep psychological scars. Moreover, in the absence of their parents, children are exposed to various social vices and feel the absence of love and care. The elderly, too, feel left out and neglected.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//98790e48-ae4d-4427-bd6d-70bd421ac0c7/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_114_810_202_892.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2Fdeffca60468d7ff4b121487fba6be9a28de3d0a27e21109676b9fc6230595c08" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>


##### Think and Answer

What are some of the social and economic impacts of rural-urban migration on both rural areas and urban cities in India?

#### BRAIN DRAIN

Brain drain is a term that refers to a situation when highly qualified and trained people leave their country to work and settle permanently in another country that offers them better job opportunities and lifestyle. It is also known as human capital flight.

##### Causes of Brain Drain

Both the push factors and the pull factors mentioned earlier are responsible for brain drain. Examples of push factors that cause

brain drain include economic factors such as the inability to find suitably paying jobs in a person's own country, poverty and no prospect of improving one's standard of living. Other factors include political instability that causes uncertainty, political favouritism and religious and social discrimination. The pull factors include higher income and more comfortable lifestyles in the new country; better economic prospects; better educational opportunities, including training and research; greater chances of promotion without partiality or discrimination; a liberal and stable government; better working conditions and medical facilities.

Rural to urban migration has been a common trend in the past 50 years in India, with people leaving their villages and relocating to towns and cities. Discuss some of the reasons behind this migration phenomenon.

Skills: Discussions and Debate

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//98790e48-ae4d-4427-bd6d-70bd421ac0c7/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_649_548_1153_638.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2Fda6d4d28ccdc2bc65dd05895f5cd0d3dfbbdc22a531b07f048e31e80db4600ee" alt="Image" width="42%" /></div>


##### Impact of Brain Drain

Brain drain has some positive as well as negative impacts on societies.

##### Positive impact

Some of the positive impacts include:

- Better employment opportunities for educated and skilled workers that may be available in their own country.

The migrant's country will prosper as money (foreign exchange) will enter the country.

- Migrants returning home will invest in their own businesses and thereby boost development and employment in the country.

- There will be greater technology transfer greater investments and capital brought back by the diaspora (groups of people)

who have moved from their own countries and settled abroad) returning home.

#### Negative impact

Some of the negative effects include:

A net decrease in the country of people with professional and technological qualifications.

The reduction of qualified and technical people in the country will impact the development and growth of the nation.

Remittances may taper off after some time as prices may increase.

Government and private scholarships to study abroad will cause drainage of talent and skills in the country.

• Reduced quality of essential services of health and education in the migrant's home country.

- With migrants returning home with plenty of money, a vast disparity can develop between the incomes of the locals and the migrants.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//f0ae551c-a0c0-4e79-b52e-cd02305dd23d/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_564_61_655_146.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A26Z%2F-1%2F%2Fbeb32fa080c1242a4a3f48a4e7f03d03957d777aff8ab8e31e86554f7a1e59eb" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>


##### Knowledge of India

In the last few years, the Indian government has taken several steps to tackle the issue of brain drain and mitigate its impact on the country. One significant initiative is the promotion of higher education and research institutions within the country. By starting some new educational institutions, such as new ITs (Indian Institute of Technology) and AllMs (All India Institute of Medical Sciences), the government aims to create an environment that promotes innovation and provides attractive opportunities for talented individuals to pursue higher education and take up employment within the country. Also, various scholarships and financial incentives have been given to encourage students and researchers to stay in India and contribute to its growth and development.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//f0ae551c-a0c0-4e79-b52e-cd02305dd23d/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_573_758_643_819.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A26Z%2F-1%2F%2F3315a4a80ea34ee23f421e025708a5cef96e089a03e41a2808ce4bd2d396126f" alt="Image" width="5%" /></div>

#### Biography

In 1876, 1885 and 1889, Ernst Georg Ravenstein, an Anglo-German geographer, published papers on internal and international migration in Britain, Europe and North America. Ravenstein outlined a series of 'laws of migration' that attempted to explain and predict migration patterns both within and between nations. His work laid the foundation for early, primarily economic studies of migration.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//f0ae551c-a0c0-4e79-b52e-cd02305dd23d/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_883_1375_1086_1598.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A26Z%2F-1%2F%2F9792c364b440418e34386e4c3972e9d6bceb6aa13fab594572610fbb3c4c85d2" alt="Image" width="17%" /></div>

##### Important Terms

Emigrant: A person who leaves his or her country to live in another

immigrant: A person who has come to live in a country that is not his or her own

Persecute: To treat somebody in a cruel and unfair way, especially because of their race, religion or political beliefs

Sect: A small group of people who belong to a particular religion but who have some beliefs or practices which separate them from the rest of the group

Repression: The act of using force to control a group of people and restrict their freedom

Remittance: As sum of money that is sent to somebody in order to pay for something

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//f0ae551c-a0c0-4e79-b52e-cd02305dd23d/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_779_401_1035_480.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2F7202d99ed741fb3124a8047ed91ecd214278427779abf9348d43118a932a7687" alt="Image" width="21%" /></div>


Modern humans (Homo sapiens) have been migrating across the earth ever since the first group moved out of Africa some 60,000 years ago. How far they went and where they settled down depended on factors such as climate, availability of water and fertile land, ability to live with others, etc.

##### Let's Do Something

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//f0ae551c-a0c0-4e79-b52e-cd02305dd23d/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_34_817_72_865.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2Fe460f5589e8eefb7a1ed1453c2c3f0091e89ab3fa3134c674dad2a572ce3c8dc" alt="Image" width="3%" /></div>


A. Debate: In groups of five, teacher will organize a debate on the topic, 'People from our neighbouring countries in South Asia, such as Myanmar, Bangladesh and Sri Lanka, who are facing serious economic distress should be allowed to easily immigrate to India for a better life.' One group should speak in favour of and the other against the topic. Each group will get a chance to ask three questions to the other group. The teacher will moderate the discussion and conclude the debate.

# Urbanization

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//5e1b7473-277c-4260-855c-06e8de4fd31d/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_162_357_248_448.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A26Z%2F-1%2F%2F83be343b0508876a7f04928a342e913aeb97dc4379939ebdda53dfe534b19fa1" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>


#### Learning Outcomes

##### The learner:

 $ ^{n} $ describes the term urbanization.

» identifies causes of urbanization.

» describes impacts of urbanization.

» differentiates a smart city from any other urban centre.

explains strategies/steps taken at the local level to keep the urban areas clean.

discusses ways to reduce the negative impact of urbanization.

##### Recall

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//5e1b7473-277c-4260-855c-06e8de4fd31d/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_411_679_479_744.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A26Z%2F-1%2F%2Fb1bf5fcd547bd66527ad4c82bdcca6457287d59b786f476971a3cd5e549c37e9" alt="Image" width="5%" /></div>


##### Skill: Communication

You have read about urbanization in history in class 6. Discuss if the urbanization that took place in ancient times was similar to the one that is there in modern times.

Urbanization is a process in which populations from rural areas move to urban areas, thus leading to the growth of towns and cities. It also leads to a progressive increase in the number of people living in towns and cities. This large-scale movement of people from rural to urban areas is largely influenced by the fact that cities and towns have better economic, political, and social benefits compared to the rural areas.

In both developing and developed countries, people move to cities and towns because they see rural areas as places of hardship and primitive lifestyle. Majority of people are attracted to towns and cities because they want to acquire better social and economic services and benefits which exist in these places. Some of the advantages of living in towns and cities are better health facilities, education, sanitation, housing, and business opportunities, entertainment facilities, clubs, restaurants, shopping malls and transportation. Therefore, as population move from backward areas to more developed areas (towns and cities), large areas of the country become urbanized.

In India, the expansion of cities increased at alarming rate. In 1901, as per the census taken the urban population was 11.4 per cent of the population. A hundred years later, by 2001, urban population had grown to 28.53 per cent and by 2021 it had become about 35 per cent, as expected that by 2030, the urban population will become around 40 per cent, according to the United Nations estimates.

##### CAUSES OF URBANIZATION

There are many factors responsible for urbanization of a place.

The dearth of jobs in villages and the lack of opportunities to earn a livelihood draw people from the rural areas to the cities.

Rapid industrial growth in and around the city provides plenty of job opportunities.

Cities also provide opportunities for unskilled workers from rural areas. They take up jobs at construction sites or as mechanics, drivers, barbers, newspaper vendors, street food sellers, etc. Such jobs or small trade opportunities are not available in villages.

Cities offer better medical facilities and healthcare services. This decreases mortality rates and causes a natural increase in population.

Cities also offer better education prospects for migrants and their children.

Cities offer higher wages to workers, a part of which they send to their families back home.

Cities offer people more varied options for recreation and entertainment, such as cinema, plays, sporting events, circuses, song or dance performances, fairs and exhibitions, etc.

Cities provide better communication and transport facilities.

Modern conveniences, improved lifestyles and freedom from rigid social norms such as the caste system that are more widely prevalent in the rural areas of India, force people to leave their villages and move to cities.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//5e1b7473-277c-4260-855c-06e8de4fd31d/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_13_712_1093_1675.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2F3a5653860921beae79f60d08391e475b3e56aa26a11c5cdd67e14ce30aaf077b" alt="Image" width="90%" /></div>


World: Urbanization

### Did You Know?

As per World Bank data, India's urban population was 508.37 million in 2022. This was about 35 per cent of India's total population. This is expected to increase to 675 million by 2035.

Discuss some strategies that can be implemented to reduce the negative impact of urbanization on the environment, infrastructure, and quality of life in rapidly growing cities. C-6.3

### IMPACT OF URBANIZATION

A large number of people migrate from rural to urban areas as a consequence of the push factors and the pull factors. While certain factors in rural areas push out people, there are some factors in urban areas that attract people. As more and more people are pushed from rural to urban areas, there are both positive and negative impacts on the people who have migrated to the city.

#### Positive Impacts of Urbanization

Urbanization has some notable positive effects on the lives of people living in big cities.

- There is development and expansion of essential services like clean water, electricity and transport in cities.

People in urban areas have greater access to health, educational, cultural and social services than in rural areas.

More schools, colleges, training centers and universities are found in urban areas which provide children of migrants with better prospects for the future.

• Availability of multifarious employment opportunities that draw younger generations from the rural areas.

- Urbanization creates harmony among people coming from different strata of society, allowing people of different castes, groups, languages and religions to live and work together in peace, thereby breaking down the social and cultural barriers.

Urbanization allows people to acquire modern communication skills. Knowledge of computers and smartphones, as well as knowledge of new languages enable many people to take up jobs that utilize these skills. Thousands of youths have found jobs in all centres across many Indian cities owing to their skills in spoken and written English.

Urbanization provides people with the opportunity to acquire training and work experience in high-tech industries and the city's 'Silicon Valleys', enhancing their skills and facilitating them to migrate to other developed countries.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//5e1b7473-277c-4260-855c-06e8de4fd31d/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_620_862_1164_1248.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2F4af5594ae70f18ff141ed547b2a21df52683c3dd370e28334c03e283df6b9c69" alt="Image" width="45%" /></div>


Urbanization provided people opportunities to work in high-tech industries.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//5e1b7473-277c-4260-855c-06e8de4fd31d/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_628_1336_695_1408.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2Fc4e5e9edcd1c5859a99c27745b6360c7e56d56cebb3432bfdbe097737b90ec88" alt="Image" width="5%" /></div>


##### Quick Facts

Bengaluru is one of the fastest-growing cities in Asia. It has become the centre of technology. Approximately 35 per cent of the professional workers are engaged in IT and related industries in Bengaluru.

#### Negative Impacts of Urbanization

Despite its many benefits, urbanization also has quite a few drawbacks.

Due to a large number of people moving in the urban areas, there is an acute shortage of housing. Many people can only afford a very small accommodation of about one room unit without any space for a toilet or kitchen.

Many people who leave their village and migrate to cities in search of a better life and occupational opportunities end up as casual labourers. They do not earn enough to be able to afford proper housing facilities in a city. This leads to the creation of slums. Slums are urban areas that are heavily populated with poor housing and living conditions.

Since slums are usually located on land not owned by the slum dwellers, they can be easily evicted (thrown out) from their houses by the owners.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//5e1b7473-277c-4260-855c-06e8de4fd31d/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_16_869_539_1265.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F40943a6420c3d418254e08840487087f001e487a9a262cc2231fb280d59db86a" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>


4 Urbanization leads to the creation of slums which have poor living conditions.

• Growth of slums in urban areas puts pressure on essential utilities such as clean drinking water, sanitation, power, etc.

• Overcrowding in slums leads to the outbreak of diseases such as malaria and dengue.

Overcrowding in cities also leads to the problem of transportation. There is poor network of roads, inadequate public transport, which leads to traffic jams and further adds to the suffering of the people commuting.

With the daily influx of a large number of people into cities who have come in search of jobs, unemployment in cities increases as the number of people looking for jobs is more than the jobs available.

Unemployment and poverty force people to engage in anti-social activities. Crimes begin to increase in slum areas, thereby making it difficult to enforce law and order.

- With the increase in urbanization, the environment is affected in many ways.

There is a steep rise in air pollution as more and more factories are built and more and more motor vehicles ply on the roads.

- A rise in air pollution leads to a consequential rise in allergies and respiratory diseases.

- Work efficiency decreases as people spend more time on travelling to and from the place of work, the time that could be spent more constructively in the office.

- Because of such factors, there will be a greater demand for online work, which will keep people apart, leading to lack of social communication.

The expansion of cities leads to the destruction of flora and fauna. With an increase in population, there is a consequent demand for more housing. In building high-rise apartments a lot of forests and wetlands are destroyed, driving away many birds and animals from their natural habitats.

In many areas close to the sea, urbanization damages the ocean ecosystem.

- Destruction of green areas and increase in built-up areas lead to an increase in city temperatures.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//5e1b7473-277c-4260-855c-06e8de4fd31d/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_135_179_222_258.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F0751379af5637b70400c84288f8045970358d5de8f0e7a400ed00258dd01761b" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>


##### Think and Answer

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//5e1b7473-277c-4260-855c-06e8de4fd31d/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_468_157_634_266.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2Faed984116c7846fa4a949329269409d0d25e5431f868865c38a9e7207c9203bc" alt="Image" width="13%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//5e1b7473-277c-4260-855c-06e8de4fd31d/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_2_1283_119_1618.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2F39a355a02b7a0fd18807d868087fa33eefdaa1d4ce4d01995bf24b86dfc2daeb" alt="Image" width="9%" /></div>


We know that most jobs are in urban areas so people move to urban areas from rural areas in search of jobs. However, it is also a fact that this leads to unbalanced national development. How do you think this problem should be addressed? C-6.4

### Ways to Reduce the Negative Impact of Urbanization

There are various steps that the government can take to check and reduce the negative effects of urbanization.

##### Sustainable and environment-friendly cities

The government should plan and provide environment-friendly cities with smart growth techniques and should pass laws to this effect. It is quite unhealthy for people to reside in unsafe and polluted areas. Therefore, the government should aim to build sustainable cities with improved environmental conditions and habitats, which are safe and clean for people living in urban areas. Governments should also encourage investment in green infrastructure, promote eco-friendly industries, emphasize on recycling and environmental campaigns, suggest ways for pollution management, provide renewable sources of energy, eco-friendly public transportation, and suggest methods of water recycling and land reclamation. The government must encourage people to use EVs (Electric Vehicles) and the use of electric buses, trams and metro trains.

##### Provision of essential services

The government at the local level must ensure that all populations living within the

urban areas have access to adequate essential services such as education, health, sanitation and clean water, technology, electricity and food. Jobs and earning opportunities must be provided so that people can earn a living and lead a good quality life. Subsidies should also be provided by the government so that the costs of basic healthcare, education, public transportation, communication systems, energy and technology can be reduced.

##### More job creation

More employment opportunities should be created to lessen the negative impact of rapid urbanization. Private investment should be encouraged in order to effectively utilize natural resources and create more job opportunities. For example, by exploiting natural resources optimally and promoting tourism, more job opportunities can be created for the urban population. In order to encourage job creation, subsidies and grants should be provided to foreign and private investment in environment-friendly development projects.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//5e1b7473-277c-4260-855c-06e8de4fd31d/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_676_961_770_1048.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2F104410a0d26f917928cfb61ee78c50b7684b1b01aff4133af9172a428e5a7c36" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>


##### Knowledge of India

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//5e1b7473-277c-4260-855c-06e8de4fd31d/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_1057_960_1170_1039.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2Fac337058dcf7cc4024f4af4da7fd59a96813c494c949530b2efaf824d49ba053" alt="Image" width="9%" /></div>


Heritage City Development and Augmentation

Yojana or HRIDAY was launched by the Ministry of Housing and Urban Affairs in 2015 to promote preservation and revitalization of the rich cultural heritage of the country. The scheme aims to conserve heritage and an inclusive sustainable development of the heritage sites, by focusing not just on the monuments, but also its citizens, tourists and local business. Some of the cities selected for the scheme are Ajmer, Amritsar, Amaravati, Warangal, Puri, Kanchipuram, Varanasi and Velankanni.

### Population control

The government at the local level in urban areas must provide medical health clinics and family planning centres to help reduce the high rates of population growth. Effective medical counselling and campaigns directed towards healthcare and hygiene and family planning options must be provided across the entire urban area with the sole purpose of controlling diseases and population growth.

#### SATELLITE CITIES

Satellite cities are smaller cities located close to a larger or main city. A satellite city can operate independent of the large city. It, however, remains essentially a part of the large urban area with the main city at the centre. With the expansion of the main city and the burden of over-utilization on its various services, the government and the city planners have to decide on ways to relieve the pressure on the main city. Often, this is done by developing another smaller town or city located close to the main city and yet completely independent of it.

Satellite towns or cities are socially and economically independent, either completely or partially. They have their own shopping centers, vegetable and meat markets, clubs, cinema halls, museums, nursing homes, hospitals, fire brigades and other services.

Some of the features of a satellite city arc:

- It is smaller than the main city and is located close to it.

• Satellite cities are separated from the main city by a wide corridor of rural land or a green belt or even a river. In the course of time, satellite cities develop their own urban areas and have their own municipalities.

• Satellite cities are well connected to the main town by metro rails, buses, motorways etc. Example: Navi Mumbai has its own airport.

• Many satellite towns or cities do not encourage the setting up of high-pollution generating industries and factories.

• Satellite towns and cities encourage development of small-scale industries such as dairy farms, cottage industries, handicraft industries, jam factories, etc.

• Satellite cities are mostly 'bedroom communities' or residential areas. People go to work in the main city and return to their homes in the satellite cities.

Some examples of satellite cities in India are:

Main City: New Delhi—Satellite cities are Gurugram and Noida.

Main City: Mumbai—Satellite cities are Navi Mumbai and Thane.

Main City: Kolkata—Satellite cities are Rajarhat and Salt Lake City.

Main City: Hyderabad—Satellite city is Hightech city.

Main City: Pune—Satellite city is Pimpri-Chinchwad.

##### CONCEPT OF SMART CITIES

What are smart cities? While the definition of a smart city is still evolving, a few things have become clear. Smart cities leverage information and communication technologies to enhance service levels, citizen well-being, sustainability and economic development including overall infrastructure, market viability and essential services to residents.

Other features of smart cities are as follows:

• They are usually compact in size.

- They use information and communication technologies to increase operational

efficiency and share information with the public.

- It is an urban region that is highly advanced in terms of overall structure, sustainable real estate, communication and market viability.

Their economy, environment, governance, human capital (labour) international outreach, mobility, transportation management, social cohesion, technology and urban planning are taken into consideration while planning and developing. A smart city, therefore, is a highly advanced entity in all these areas.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//98824a4a-c47b-4f8a-bef0-109e2eabad2c/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_123_550_645_894.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2Fa77fcef9e5c4ecd024ff5564b5cd9e590ce89091ad687025a685ed7362b21820" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>


Smart cities are urban regions that are highly advanced in terms of overall infrastructure.

- These cities have more effective data-driven decision-making.

- They have enhanced citizen and government engagement and deliver robust user-friendly digital services.

They have safer communities as technology helps reduce criminal activities by installing CCTV cameras at very close distances.

- With the rise of greenhouse gases, trashes in the streets, debris in the oceans, smart cities help reduce the negative effects on the environment. Planners ensure energy efficient buildings, install air quality sensors and renewable energy resources.

• They have improved and efficient transport systems throughout.

#### Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs)

##### Goal 6: Clean Water and Sanitation

The Atal Mission for Rejuvenation and Urban Transformation (AMRUT) is a national urban renewal programme of the Government of India. The programme aims to improve the quality of life in urban areas. It aims to improve basic amenities such as water supply, sewerage and stormwater drainage. It also aims to improve the urban environment by promoting green spaces and public transportation.

• They have efficient public utilities with limited supply of natural resources to meet human demand and provide tools needed to effectively conserve and use water and electricity.

They ensure adequate green cover and ensure a sustainable environment.

The main purpose of a smart city is to improve the quality of life of the people; harnessing information technology and push economic growth. Also, smart cities encourage area-based development by transforming existing areas, including slums into better-planned places so that people live happily and comfortably. New areas are identified in such cities so that more people can be accommodated in the future.

In India, 100 cities (as of 2023) have already been selected as 'Smart Cities' as part of the Smart Cities Mission. The mission includes Bhubaneswar, Jaipur, Surat, Pune, Lucknow, Chandigarh, Hyderabad, Vadodara, Kochi, Visakhapatnam, Guwahati, Raipur, Bilaspit, Durgapur, Indore, Gwalior, Rourkeh, Jabalpur and Bhopal.

According to the 2023 Smart City Index, which was published by The Smart City Observation (a part of the Swiss Business School Institute for Management Development or DMC Zurich is ranked first, Oslo second and Canberra grabbed the third spot.

g. Helsinki, Finland

The data was collected from over 20,000 citizens, who were queried on the following points: affordable housing, road congestion, green spaces, fulfilling employment needs, structures and technologies built to address their concerns and how comfortable the respondents were with technologies such as face recognition and sharing personal data to improve traffic congestion.
