##### PHYSICAL FEATURES

Asia is broadly divided into five physical regions:

• The Northern Lowlands

- The Central Fold Mountains and Inter-montane Plateaux

• The Southern Plateaux

The Great River Valleys

The Island Chains

##### The Northern Lowlands

This stretch of low-lying land extends from the Ural mountains in the west up to the Bering Strait in the north-east. These lowlands, which are triangular in shape, are the widest in the west. Lying between the Arctic Ocean in the north and the Central Mountains in the south, they form the world's greatest continuous plains. Three rivers which flow northwards into the Arctic Ocean, namely rivers Ob, Yenisey and Lena, have together built this plain. Also known as the Great Siberian Plain, these are marshy and swampy lowlands. The lower courses and mouths of the rivers freeze in winter. So, water coming from the upper courses, which are situated in warmer latitudes, spreads out over large parts of the plains. Another lowland region of a smaller extent exists south of the Siberian Plains in Central Asia around the Aral Sea.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//46c64e33-ba77-4478-b468-389e40bc7691/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_126_1160_662_1525.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A30Z%2F-1%2F%2F40c035fa16c30448e7aad4ee3632347902dfa75ea7d0534d21320a563b078ec2" alt="Image" width="45%" /></div>


An aerial view of the vast plains in Siberia, Russia

This plain is an area of the drainage known as the Turan Plain. It is drained by the Turan Amu Darya and Syr Darya.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//46c64e33-ba77-4478-b468-389e40bc7691/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_655_153_724_217.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A30Z%2F-1%2F%2F59198434a838b82c0e92f694a6fe22e786da1bf3669626875b14f1d6640dddb1" alt="Image" width="5%" /></div>


#### SWII: CTHSI THIMA

How has the geography and abundance of resources of the Northern Lowlands influenced human settlements, transportation, agriculture, and natural resource extraction in the region?

### The Central Fold Mountains and Inter-montane Plateaux

A complex system of fold mountain ranges with some plateau in between the ranges found in the region south of the Northern Lowlands of Asia. A close look at this system shows several mountain ranges meeting in a small zone that has been named the Pamir Knot. From the Pamir Knot, several mountain ranges appear to radiate outward in different directions.

##### Discuss

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//46c64e33-ba77-4478-b468-389e40bc7691/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_673_822_1166_911.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A30Z%2F-1%2F%2F95e306d70325e42d65653c9266a061cfd95f6286e93e5bbc1c840d5429092f10" alt="Image" width="41%" /></div>


What are the ways in which the mountains are useful to us?

To the east and the north of the Pami Knot, extend the Kunlun and the Tien Shan mountains, respectively. The Himalayas emerge from the Pamir Knot and extend in a south-easterly direction as a wide arc across the northern extent of India. They then turn southwards into Myanmar as the Arakam. Youna Range. The Karakoram Range is a short range which extends south-eastward from the Pamir Knot between the Kunlun and the Himalayas. Some of the world's highest peaks are found in these ranges. The Plateau of Tibet is an inter-montane plateau-plateau located between mountain ranges which lies between the Kunlun and the Himalayas.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//46c64e33-ba77-4478-b468-389e40bc7691/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_43_0_1101_987.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2Ffbf058b24080ba3b61f80c0333311393b6fea11c81d18e6bbec336ec8d28386a" alt="Image" width="88%" /></div>


1 Physical map of Asia

The Altai, Yablonovy and Stanovoy mountain ranges extend in a north-easterly direction beyond the Tien Shan up to the extreme north-eastern corner of Asia. The Khingan mountains just north of the Huang Bay Basin extend in a north-south direction almost parallel to the coast.

To the west of the Pamir Knot, the Hindu Kush Range continues further westward as the Elburz Mountains. The Sulaiman Range radiates south-westward from the Pamirs and continues as the Kirthar and the Zagros ranges. These mountains enclose the Plateau of Iran and they converge at another smaller knot called the Armenian Knot.

Two mountain ranges, the Pontic in the north and the Taurus in the south, radiate westward from this knot. These two ranges are to the south of the Black Sea. They enclose the Plateau of Anatolia between them.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//46c64e33-ba77-4478-b468-389e40bc7691/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_576_1262_684_1347.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F21aeb6096d054d829bc5739457f0e103555b37eb6e7a2627956ca88361ed69aa" alt="Image" width="9%" /></div>


#### Did You Know?

The Plateau of Tibet is also called the 'Roof of the World' as it is the highest flat land in the world at an average height of 4,880 m above sea level.

The Central Mountains and Plateaux have been formidable physical and political barriers. Gaps or passes in these mountains,

such as the Khyber, Bolan, and Solan Passes, allow the movement of goods and people across the mountains.

Mt Everest (8848.86 m) in the Himalayas is the highest peak in the world and Mt K2 or Godwin Austin (8,611 m) in the Karakoram Range is the world's second highest peak. There are several peaks over 8,000 m high in these ranges. Also, some of the largest glaciers in the world are found here such as the Siachen and Baltoro glaciers.

##### The Southern Plateaux

The Arabian Plateau, the Deccan Plateau, and the Shan and Yunnan Plateaux lic in the region south of the Central Mountains and Inter-montane plateaux. These are regions of old, hard crystalline rocks which are at some height above sea level. Their surfaces are undulating and gently sloping.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//46c64e33-ba77-4478-b468-389e40bc7691/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_90_852_640_1211.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2F2657c7827408583c7b33ef663d29f37a679ce633ce0889087477dbfc47329473" alt="Image" width="46%" /></div>


Dry hills in the Deccan Plateau region of India

The Arabian Plateau is steeper in the west but gently slopes eastward towards the Persian Gulf. It is a dry plateau as it is in the region of low rainfall and has no rivers. The Deccan Plateau of India lies between the Western Ghats and the Eastern Ghats. It is steeper and higher along the Arabian Sea in the west but slopes gently towards the Bay of Bengal in the east. A number of rivers flow across this

plateau. Can you name these rivers? The Shan Plateau in Myanmar and the Yunnan Plateau in China further east are drained by the rivers Salween, Mekong, and Si Kiang.

##### The Great River Valleys

Several large rivers rise in the mountains and plateaux of Asia. These rivers are mostly snow-fed and perennial. The valleys of these rivers are very fertile and are, therefore, densely populated. The larger river valleys are those built by the rivers Tigris, Euphrates, Indus, Ganga, Brahmaputra, Chao Phraya.

#### Some Important Rivers of Asia

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//7aa909dd-d563-49bd-b1c1-25e594a83b4e/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_894_10_1041_93.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A26Z%2F-1%2F%2F9a4c089e7839400ed2c2f736c5cd8fe90c19cd23c9efbb100bd35893d1fc5a8e" alt="Image" width="12%" /></div>


India has a wealth of rich knowledge and diverse culture. Birthplace of Hinduism, Buddhism and Sikhism, it is famous for landmarks such as the Konark Sun Temple, the Taj Mahal, and geographical features such as the Himalayas and the backwaters of Kerala. With a growing economy and recent successes in 2023 like the Chandrayaan-3 and the hosting of the G20 Summit, India has a prominent role in Asia's political and economic landscape.

groups of islands extend in an arc, forming archipelagoes. From the tip of the Kamchatka Peninsula in the Pacific Ocean onward, these are the Kuril Islands, the Japanese Islands (Hokkaido, Honshu, Shikoku and Kyushu), the Ryukyu Islands, the Philippines, and the Indonesian Islands. The Andaman and Nicobar Islands, Sri Lanka, the Maldives, and the Lakshadweep Islands are in South Asia.

#### Biography

Vasco da Gama (1460–1524 CE) was a Portuguese navigator who was the first to sail from Europe to India by rounding Africa's Cape of Good Hope. He made many stops in Africa before reaching the trading post of Calicut (now Kozhikode), India, on May 20, 1498 CE. This journey was crucial in establishing a direct sea route to Asia, which was highly sought after by European explorers during the Age of Exploration. The sea route allowed for a more efficient trade and access to valuable goods from Asia, such as spices and textiles.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//7aa909dd-d563-49bd-b1c1-25e594a83b4e/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_908_342_1122_557.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A26Z%2F-1%2F%2F11afd89d1f70f1125bc4568a9436fcdb5c36a305836e4703c441c9e8e64aad06" alt="Image" width="17%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//7aa909dd-d563-49bd-b1c1-25e594a83b4e/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_7_602_1177_1651.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A26Z%2F-1%2F%2F2903002223a87b61bac17c6cc0e6ec9d36844850ff56f83ec29f28c62b1a2112" alt="Image" width="98%" /></div>


### Important Terms

Eurasia: The land mass of Europe and Asia as a whole

Snow-fed rivers: Rivers that receive water from melting snow

Perennial rivers: Rivers that flow throughout the year, even in the dry season

Archipelago: A group of islands

## 2. Read the following passage and answer the questions.

(iii) Where are most of Indonesia's islands located?

Indonesia is an archipelagic country located in Asia. It is the world's largest archipelago, consisting of around 17,000 islands that span the equator, situated between the continents of Asia and Australia. The majority of Indonesia's islands are located near the equator. Indonesia is known for its volcanic and seismic activity due to its location along the Pacific Ring of Fire. It has a high number of active volcanoes, making it prone to volcanic eruptions and earthquakes.

##### Recall

##### Skill: Communication

Why is the climate of a place important? Discuss.

In the previous chapter you read about the physical features of Asia. Let us now look at its climate.

#### Factors that Affect the Climate of Asia

#### CLIMATE

The climate of Asia varies greatly from north to south and east to west. This, in turn, large effects the vegetation and wildlife of the continent. Not only are there variations from place to place, but also from season to season. There are several factors that affect the climate of Asia. Let us study the table below.

Asia is the largest continent with a large east-west extent. Also, it stretches across the temperate and frigid zones of the earth.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a5059809-23ac-449f-a5d5-ede8a2728d0c/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_7_890_251_1681.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2F979022583e50f9e01aa7252c6aa59fd8d123573e7fdb207a9d3cb91a9e9487a2" alt="Image" width="20%" /></div>


Most of the interior parts are away from seas and oceans. These areas experience extremes conditions and continental climate.

• Places closer to the coasts enjoy equable or maritime climate.

Most of the mountain ranges of Asia extend in an east-west direction. They form bari to the on-shore moisture-bearing winds from the south and also prevent the cold winds of the north from penetrating the south.

Mountains create rain shadows, leading to variations in precipitation and temperaturit either side.

Plateaus and plains have distinct climatic characteristics, like the cold Tibetan Plateau

Coastal regions benefit from moderating effects of nearby bodies of water, while islands and deserts have unique micro-climates. Monsoons, driven by relief-induced temperature differences, play a vital role, bringing seasonal rains to many parts of Asia.

Monsoon winds are a critical climatic factor in Asia, especially in South and South-and Asia. These seasonal wind patterns, influenced by temperature contrasts between land and ocean, bring heavy rainfall in the wet season and dry conditions in the dry season. Monsoons are vital for agriculture, and impact water resources.

The cold Oya Siwo Oyashio and the warm Kuro Siwo Kuroshio (Japanese Black curren ocean currents affect the temperatures of the coastal regions of Japan.

The mixing of the cold Oya Siwo and the warm Kuro Siwo ocean currents provides suitable temperatures for the breeding of fish, which is why the Sea of Japan is one of the best fishing grounds of the world.

Asia has several very hot and very cold places. It also has the wettest and the driest places in the world. Mawsynram in India has an annual rainfall of about 1,187 cm, while in the urban and Gobi Deserts and Tibet, the rainfall is less than 25 cm.

### summer Conditions

From April to June, the sun's rays fall directly over the northern hemisphere. In June, it shines overhead the Tropic of Cancer, so most of the continent of Asia, except the extreme northern parts beyond the Arctic Circle, is warm, with an average temperature of about  $ 32^{\circ} $C. In fact, the world's highest surface temperature of  $ 71^{\circ} $C has been recorded in Dasht-e Lut in Iran.

The hot air over the land rises and creates an area of low pressure. There is high pressure in

the surrounding seas and oceans. Therefore, there is a movement of warm, moisture-laden onshore winds which are called monsoons. These winds cause heavy rainfall in the southern part of Asia, in countries such as India, Sri Lanka, Myanmar, Thailand, Malaysia, Indonesia, Laos, Vietnam, China and some parts of Japan. Mawsynram in Meghalaya receives the heaviest rainfall in the world.

#### Winter Conditions

From October to March, Asia experiences winter as the northern hemisphere receives the slanting rays of the sun because of the tilt of the earth's axis. The temperature falls to  $ 0^{\circ} $C and even below freezing point in many parts of northern Asia. Verkhoyansk in Russia, with an average temperature of  $ -51^{\circ} $C in January, is one of the world's coldest inhabited places. The air over the land is cold

Asia: Rainfall and Winds

and heavy and, therefore, sinks, causing high pressure, especially in the interior.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a5059809-23ac-449f-a5d5-ede8a2728d0c/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_91_196_621_564.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2F44e52934a1743927aa8925a37e441ed287c3af993754c84e62818315c8f9143e" alt="Image" width="44%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">▲ Verkhoyansk is one of the world's coldest inhabited places.</div> </div>


The surrounding oceans and seas have higher temperature and lower pressure. Thus, there is movement of cold air from land to sea. These winds are dry and they blow offshore, so most of Asia receives no winter rainfall, except southeast Asia, Japan, south-eastern India and parts of northern Sri Lanka, where the same winds cross the seas and pick up moisture before reaching these places. A few regions of south-west Asia receive winter rainfall from the topsperate cyclones that originate over the Mediterranean Sea. Owing to the various factors discussed above, Asia has different types of climate and consequently, a great variety of vegetation and wildlife species. These have been discussed in detail here.

##### TYPES OF CLIMATE

##### Equatorial Climate

This is experienced in countries located close to the equator—Malaysia, Indonesia and southern Philippines. The countries have high temperatures of about  $ 28^{\circ}-30^{\circ} $C and rainfall all year round. The annual range of temperature is very low and there are no distinct seasons. Convectional rainfall occurs almost daily around 4 o'clock in this region.

##### Natural vegetation and wildlife

The climatic conditions have resulted in dense hardwood forests, with broadleaved tree species such as mahogany, ebony, rosewood, cinchona, coconut and rubber. There are lianas, creepers and climbers, tall grass, ferns and bamboo that grow between the tall trees, which make the forests dense and impenetrable. The forests are dark and gloomy as very little sunlight reaches the ground owing to the tall trees whose branches spread out, forming a canopy.

These forests are slightly different from the rainforests of the Amazon and Zaire basins because of their nearness to the sea. Mostly arboreal or tree-dwelling animals such as monkeys, apes and colourful birds are found in these forests. Reptiles such as lizards, snakes, crocodiles and insects abound the swampy floors of the forests. Large animals such as elephants and wild cats are only found in the outskirts as the forest interior is too dense.

##### Tropical Monsoon Climate

These areas have distinct seasons—hot wet summers and cool dry winters. The summer rainfall is caused by the monsoon winds that blow from the sea to land. Heavier rainfall is received in the coastal regions and on the windward slopes. This type of climate is experienced in India, Pakistan, Bangladesh, Myanmar, Thailand, Vietnam, Laos, Cambodia and southern China.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a5059809-23ac-449f-a5d5-ede8a2728d0c/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_658_1321_755_1400.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2F6fbdba94f7646803d7a23771626c4e786d42b993be55a5d09e9bdca25f6590d2" alt="Image" width="8%" /></div>


##### Did You Know?

The monsoon still remains a complex weather phenomenon. It is difficult, even now, to accurately predict the time of its arrival and retreat, the places that will get rain and the quantity of rainfall that will be received in a year.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a5059809-23ac-449f-a5d5-ede8a2728d0c/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_79_0_949_822.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A30Z%2F-1%2F%2Fc0f70d61717eae9c29354ab9193fbc7ddd7be1375341e0793563b1d33de37b19" alt="Image" width="73%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">Asia: Climate and natural vegetation</div> </div>


### Natural vegetation and wildlife

Tropical deciduous forests called monsoons forests with hardwood, broad-leaved trees are common. These trees shed their leaves in the dry season, usually in winter. Teak, shisham and mango are the common tree species. These thrive in regions of heavy rainfall. Grasses and thorny bushes grow in different regions. Elephants, rhinoceros, bears, deer, apes, lions, tigers, leopards, etc., are some of the wildlife species found in the monsoon forests.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a5059809-23ac-449f-a5d5-ede8a2728d0c/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_32_1386_87_1476.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A30Z%2F-1%2F%2F68bafabd2e276d100449323aa7efa520a79c9838ea442e7acf18f3e3f40956f5" alt="Image" width="4%" /></div>


### Knowledge of India

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a5059809-23ac-449f-a5d5-ede8a2728d0c/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_386_1330_549_1452.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A30Z%2F-1%2F%2Ffa3a5d4257a41d9fc79004c07e84c33a3ea1064fcdb1624f2a315a3896d25373" alt="Image" width="13%" /></div>


The Western Ghats of India are home to around 325 species of flora and fauna which are considered globally threatened. This shows the rich biodiversity of the Western Ghats.

### Tropical or Hot Desert Climate

This type of climate prevails in Arabia, Iran and the Thar Desert in Pakistan and India. These regions experience very hot dry summers and very cold winters. The daily and annual ranges of temperature are very high and the areas receive less than 25 cm of rainfall annually.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a5059809-23ac-449f-a5d5-ede8a2728d0c/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_569_1159_646_1239.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A30Z%2F-1%2F%2Fab312ca98088143bc8b9d9724e245a3e9df59c80eee9efc6b321750f28c98809" alt="Image" width="6%" /></div>


What is the importance of the Himalayas for the Indian subcontinent?

## Natural vegetation and wildlife

As climatic conditions are harsh, vegetation is scarce and only thorny bushes, shrubs, cacti and clumps of dry grasses are found scattered in the region, which is largely bare and devoid of vegetation. Date palms are found in the

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a5059809-23ac-449f-a5d5-ede8a2728d0c/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_120_152_626_617.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F245e6af82cb2a7361aa67639a7838bef0575dccaed53eaa7c9254d0f2e744015" alt="Image" width="42%" /></div>


Date Palms are found in the oasis.

## Warm Temperate Eastern Margin or China-type Climate

This climate type is similar to the monsoon type, except that the winters are colder. Snowfall occurs in winter, while rainfall occurs in summer. The regions along the east coast of Asia in the warm temperate latitudes, such as northern and central China, Japan and parts of Korea experience this type of climate.

#### Natural vegetation and wildlife

Mixed forests with evergreen and deciduous trees are common. Oak, camellia, magnolia, chestnut, camphor, beech and fir are some common trees. Bamboo and mulberry shrubs also grow in this region. Monkeys, foxes and birds such as parrots, peacocks and pheasants are found mainly on the slopes of the highlands, which support these mixed forests.

### Temperate or Mid-latitude Desert Climate

This climate type is found in the interior of the continent and on high plateau—the Gobi Desert and the Plateau of Tibet. Very little rainfall is experienced and winters are very cold with temperatures below the freezing point. However, summers are very hot.

### Natural vegetation and wildlife

The region is mostly barren with scatterets, tufts of coarse, short grasses and stunted thorny bushes. Lizards, insects and rodents are the common forms of wildlife, while lyrisk is the most common domesticated animals in Tibet.

### Mediterranean Climate

This climate is characterized by warm, or summers and cool, wet winters. The climate type gets its name from the Mediterranean region around which this type of climate prevails. Countries of west Asia such as Syria, Turkiye, Lebanon and Israel have this type of climate.

#### Natural vegetation and wildlife

Since these areas experience drought-like conditions in summer, the natural vegetation has adapted to the climate by developing long roots and spongy barks. The evergreen vegetation consists of laurel and acacia. Oil chestnut, walnut and olive trees are also common. Most of the natural vegetation has been replaced by grain farms or orchards; citrus fruits, such as lemons and oranges; vineyards. Since most of the original forest cover has been cleared for human settlement or for agriculture, not much wildlife is found here. Mostly, domesticated animals such donkeys, cattle and sheep are found here.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a5059809-23ac-449f-a5d5-ede8a2728d0c/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_637_1365_1137_1473.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F802c47802df21715531c3a8e812790671d5a87006d383ab49c68de3f82610430" alt="Image" width="42%" /></div>


Do you agree that there is a relationship between a country's climate and its wealth and economic development? Provide reasons for your answer.

## temperate Grassland or Steppe climate

this climate mainly occurs around the Caspian Sea region of Russia and in eastern Mongolia. Being in the interior, far removed from the oceanic influence, these regions have extreme climatic conditions. Summers are hot and dry, while winters are cold and dry. Very little rainfall, varying from 25 to 75 cm annually is received in summer.

the steppes have short grasses and low

shes as there are temperature extremes and

very little rainfall. Antelope, horses, mules

and wolves are found here.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//21089e7c-83ff-41bf-8877-742fc198dac6/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_12_612_500_927.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F7a272a0e6f8557c569867a3a49a87c8ac851d394ca1c12ba57c9d1937d35ead1" alt="Image" width="41%" /></div>


The sieppes—the temperate grasslands of Asia

Vist stretches of the grasslands have been converted into rich farmlands that grow violet, barley and other food grains. Also, livestock rearing has become important in the region and cattle, sheep and horses are neared. The two-humped Bactrian camel is a well-known animal of this region.

### Cool Temperate Eastern Margin Climate

Cool Temperate Eastern Margin China

This type of climate is experienced in the eastern coastal regions of Asia including eastern Siberia, North China, Manchuria, parts of Korea and northern Japan. The region has cold, very dry winters, and very warm, exceptionally wet summers. Winter temperatures may be well below freezing point and snowfall may be quite high. Summers are warm as in the tropics.

#### Natural vegetation and wildlife

Heavy rainfall, warm summers, damp air and fog favour the growth of trees. The forests tend to be coniferous north of the 50° N latitude and deciduous south of this latitude. Oak, beech, maple and birch are the main trees in the south. The occurrence of these trees in almost pure stands, and the predominance of only a handful of species greatly increase the commercial value of these forests.

#### Cold Temperate Climate

The northern part of Asia, in the sub-Arctic region of north Siberia experiences long severe winters with heavy snowfall and very short, cool summers with light rainfall.

#### Natural vegetation and wildlife

The natural vegetation of the region has adapted very well to the climate. The evergreen softwood trees of the region are conical in shape and have needle-like leaves. These coniferous trees get their names from the cones in which they bear their seeds. The common tree species are pine, fir, spruce, larch and cedar. The forests are also called the taiga. They are home to several small to medium-sized fur-bearing animals such as the sable, fox, bear, mink, lynx and squirrel.

### Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs)

#### Goal 15: Life on Land

Snow leopards are found in northern and central Asia's high mountains. Their distinct features include thick fur on their body and very long tails. Unfortunately, they are hunted for their fur. Data gathered from different reliable sources indicate that 200-400 snow leopards are poached annually for illegal trade in animal body parts. The International Union for Conservation of Nature (IUCN) has listed snow leopards under the vulnerable category and is trying to conserve them and develop the communities near their habitats.

#### Arctic Climate

The Arctic climate of the tundra region, as the name implies, is mainly experienced in the regions beyond the Arctic Circle in the extreme northern shores of Asia bordering the Arctic Ocean. This region has long, extremely cold winters with heavy snowfall and temperatures below freezing point. Summers, therefore, are very short and cool with little or no rainfall.

#### Natural vegetation and wildlife

The long, severe winters and the frozen subsoil do not permit the growth of trees and this region is, therefore, devoid of forests. The tundra or the vast treeless plains, can only support a few stunted shrubs along water courses, and mosses and lichens. In summer, a few flowering plants with short life cycles bloom. Polar bears, reindeer, foxes, seals and walruses are some of the common animals found in the Arctic climatic region.

#### FORESTS

About one third of the land area of Asia is covered with forest. Some of these forests provide hardwood, bamboo, sandalwood and camphor. They also provide other valuable forest products such as lac, resin, turpentine, honey, medicinal plants and herbs. Natural rubber is obtained from the latex of the rubber tree. The evergreen rainforest of the equatorial region and the monsoon forests of the tropical regions of Asia are the chief sources of these products.

Softwood forests yield softwood for making paper, pulp, newsprint, matchsticks and synthetic fibres such as rayon. These are obtained from trees such as birch, pine, cedar and fir, which grow in the taiga or coniferous forest regions of northern Asia, especially Siberia.

#### MINERALS AND POWER RESOURCES

India, Malaysia, China, Russia, Japan, the

Philippines and North Korea have vast deposits of iron ore. Coal is found in large quantities in Asia. About half of the world reserves occur in north China, India, Kazakhstan and Siberia in Russia. The coal deposits are found near the iron ore reserves and are, therefore, helpful in settling up industries.

India, Kazakhstan, China and Russia produce manganese. Manganese is mixed with pigiri to impart hardness to steel. Large quantities of bauxite are mined in India, Indonesia and Russia. It is the ore from which aluminium is extracted. India has very large reserves of mica. This mineral is used as an insulator in the electrical industry. Tin is produced in Malaysia, China, Myanmar, Indonesia and Thailand. Gold, silver and copper deposits also occur in significant quantities in Asia.

Petroleum is an important power resource in Asia. Also called mineral oil, petroleum is refined to obtain products such as petrol, kerosene, lubricants, wax, vaseline, tar, etc. Saudi Arabia, United Arab Emirates, Bahrain, Kuwait, Iran, Iraq, India, Malaysia, Indonesia, Myanmar, China and Russia are the principal oil-producing countries of Asia.

Thermal electricity is produced by burning coal and petroleum. The force of running and falling water generates electricity known as hydroelectricity. Asia has been blessed with several large rivers which are swift-flowing and have ideal sites for power generation units. Countries such as Russia, Japan, China, Pakistan and India are using hydroelectricity significantly. However, there is vast potential for developing this resource.

#### Biography

Alexander Theodor von Middendorff was a zoologist and an explorer. His name is closely associated with the exploration of Siberia and research on the natural history of the Russian Arctic. He is known for his 1843-45 expedition to the far north and east of Siberia, which helped to understand the effects of small frost on the spread of flora and fauna.

##### Important Terms

Steppes: The temperate grasslands of Central Asia

Taiga: Coniferous forest between the temperate grasslands and the tundra

Tundra: The large, flat Arctic regions of northern Europe, Asia and North America where no trees grow and where the soil below the surface of the ground is always frozen.

Hydroelectricity: Electricity produced using the power of water

# THEME 7: INDIA—GEOGRAPHICAL FEATURES

# India—Location, Extent, Political and Physical Features

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//df03a6a6-5c35-44f4-b481-db4de3d3e868/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_26_331_76_441.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2Fe90ba9fa008f0cf84beae7379baace826010793b24b551088a1dfe6ad1af731e" alt="Image" width="4%" /></div>


### Learning Outcomes

The learner:

interprets the location and extent of India with reference to other countries of Asia.

locates important mountains, plateaus, deserts, islands and rivers on the map of India.

### Recall

##### skills: Remembering and Understanding

India forms a major part of the Indian subcontinent.

Name the countries that form the Indian subcontinent.

Geographically, India is a part of the continent of Asia. It is the seventh largest country in the world in terms of area and has the largest population in the world. However, owing to its large size and its relative isolation from the rest of Asia because of the protective barrier of the Eimalayas, it has developed its own distinct physical and cultural identity. India, Pakistan, Nepal, Bhutan, Bangladesh and Sri Lanka form a subcontinent and since India occupies the major part of the subcontinent, the entire region is called the Indian subcontinent.

#### LOCATION AND EXTENT

India lies entirely in the northern and eastern hemispheres. It extends from 8°4'N to 37°6'N latitudes and 68°7'E to 97°25'E longitudes. The Tropic of Cancer passes right through India, dividing it into two parts. The 82½°E longitude passing through Prayagraj is the Standard Meridian for India. Because of the vast east-west extent, there is a difference of

two hours in the local time of Gujarat in the west and Arunachal Pradesh in the east.

India has an approximate area of about 3.3 million sq. km. The lofty Himalayas separate it from the rest of Asia. India's neighbouring countries are Pakistan, Afghanistan, China, Nepal, Myanmar, Bangladesh and Bhutan. In the south lies the island country of Sri Lanka, which is separated from India by the Palk Strait and the Gulf of Mannar. The Maldives, which is located very close to the Lakshadweep Islands is also a neighbouring country.

##### India at a Glance



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Latitudinal extent</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>8°4′N–37°6′N</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Longitudinal extent</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>68°7′E–97°25′E</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Area</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>32,87,263 sq. km</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>North-south extent</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>3,214 km</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>East-west distance</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>2,933 km</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Length of land frontier</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>15,200 km</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Length of coastline</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>7,516.6 km</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Number of states</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>28</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Number of union territories</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>8</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Capital</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>New Delhi</td></tr></table>

South of the Tropic of Cancer lies peninsular India—a triangular mass projecting into the Indian Ocean. It is surrounded by water on three sides. The Arabian Sealies in the west, the Bay of Bengal in the east and the Indian Ocean in the south. The location of India has helped in the development of trade and commerce. The existence of seas on three sides has encouraged international trade. From ancient times, India has had political, economic and cultural links with other countries. Today, India provides a link between the east and the west. Its central position between the two worlds has helped the development of its own industries and trade.

#### POLITICAL DIVISIONS

For administrative purposes, India is divided into 28 states and 8 centrally administered union territories. The states were reorganized after Independence on the basis of language Delhi, one of the union territories, is referred to as the National Capital Territory. People of India speak different languages and have diverse cultural, religious and ethnic traits.

• The Northern Mountains

The Great Northern Plains

The Coastal Plains

The Islands

##### The Northern Mountains

The Northern Mountains consist of the Himalayas and the hills of north-east India.

Together they form the northern and north-eastern boundaries of the country.

The Himalayas, literally meaning ‘abode of snow’, form the highest mountain system in the world. The Himalayas extend from Nanga Parbat in the north-west to Namcha Barwa in Arunachal Pradesh, covering a distance of over 2,400 km. The width of this mountain arc varies between 15 and 400 km.

The Himalayas consist of three main ranges that are almost parallel. They are:

• The Greater Himalayas (Himadri)

• The Lesser Himalayas (Himachal)

The features of each of these three ranges are discussed in the table given on the next page.

The Outer Himalayas (Shiwalik)

The hills of the north-east are collectively called the Purvanchal ranges and lie along the eastern borders of India. Their average elevation is less than 3,000 m. They consist of several hill ranges such as of the Patkai Burn, Naga, Mizo, Garo, Khasi, and Jaintia Hills.

There are a number of passes or gaps in the Himalayas that serve as important passages through the northern mountain wall. Some of the important passes are Shipki La, Thaga La, Nathu La and Jelcp La.

The Himalayas exert a significant influence on the life of the people of India in several ways.

They form a natural boundary between India and China.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//df03a6a6-5c35-44f4-b481-db4de3d3e868/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_124_751_1183_1554.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2F3ed44f483b281ac978f0f4bb6a9b8c96388e0352663923145a8acbc9c9e8053a" alt="Image" width="88%" /></div>


### the Hittensack



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>They are the northernmost range of the Himalayas.</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>They lie between the Outer and the Greater Himalayas.</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>They form the foothills of the Himalayas to the south.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Maximum height: 8848.86 m</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Maximum height: 5,000 m; Width: 75 km</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Maximum height: 1,500 m</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>(Alt Everest)</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'></td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Width: 15-50 km</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Several peaks with a height of over 8,000 m. It is snow-covered throughout the year</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>The Kashmir, Kulu and Kangra valleys lie between the Lesser and the Greater Himalayas.</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Rich source of timber</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Many important rivers originate from the glaciers of the range, Gangu and Yamuna originating from Gangotri and Yamunotri glaciers, respectively.</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Popular hill stations like Darjiling, Shimla, Nainital, Mussooric are in this range.</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Have flat longitudinal valleys called Duns, covered with soft rocks mud and silt.</td></tr></table>

They serve as a climatic barrier by preventing the entry of the cold winds from Central Asia and preventing the rain-bearing monsoon winds from leaving India.

They are a source of perennial rivers such as the Indus, the Ganga and the Brahmaputra and their tributaries.

Their rugged terrain is ideal for hydroelectric power generation.

The mountain slopes are forested. These forests provide different types of timber and forest products.

The Himalayas have beautiful hill stations such as Shimla, Darjiling, Mussoorie, etc.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//ab1baae1-3869-4325-91f3-27d07130fe5c/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_17_1202_81_1285.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F644af3d32abd654997a2461b307d5cbce2b4a6a7c13633406025e13e25bb4fea" alt="Image" width="5%" /></div>


### Did You Know?

Indira Col in the Himalayas is the point where the boundaries of five countries meet. The countries are India, Pakistan, Afghanistan, China, and Tajikistan.

## The Great Northern Plains

the Great Northern Plains lie between the Northern Mountains in the north and the Peninsular Plateau of India in the south. They

extend in a great curve from Punjab in the west to the Brahmaputra Valley in the east for a length of about 2,400 km. The plains are one of the most productive and densely populated lowlands in the world. These plains have been formed by sediments deposited by the three major rivers—the Indus, the Ganga, and the Brahmaputra and their tributaries. The Great Northern Plains are of more recent origin than the Himalayas. They are also one of the largest depositional plains in the world.

The Great Northern Plains can be divided into the Ganga Plains in the centre, the Punjab Plains in the west and the Brahmaputra Valley in the east.

The alluvial soil of these plains is very fertile. The soil is constantly renewed by the silt deposited by the rivers, which spread over the land during floods.

The Ganga Plains are formed by the alluvial deposits of the river Ganga and its tributaries such as the Yamuna, the Ghaghara, the Gomti, the Gandak, the Chambal, the Betwa, and the Son. They lie in Uttar Pradesh, Bihar, and West Bengal. Their average height is between 30 and 150 m.

The Punjab Plains are formed by the alluvial deposits of the tributaries of the river Indus. They lie in Punjab and Haryana. Their average height is between 200 and 240 m.

The Brahmaputra Valley is formed by the Brahmaputra River. It lies in Assam. Its average height is 100 m. The Ganga, and the Brahmaputra join in Bangladesh, where they flow as one river—the Padma—which flows into the Bay of Bengal. Together, these rivers have built the largest delta in the world—the Sundarbans, home of Royal Bengal tigers.

The Great Northern Plains have greatly influenced the lives of the people in India in the following ways:

The fertile soil of the plains has helped in the development of agriculture.

• Its soft soil has made irrigation possible.

- Their flatness has promoted the growth and development of a dense network of road and rail transport.

- Their rivers and tributaries provide cheap water transport.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//ab1baae1-3869-4325-91f3-27d07130fe5c/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_132_925_645_998.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2F2eabc19410436eab17f6e09c466db02d452157a54d440bd2ce6b83006fb735e9" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>


The Great Northern Plains of India are most densely populated region of India. Give reasons for your answer. C-6.4

##### The Peninsular

It is an ancient land mass, made up of hard crystalline rocks of igneous and metamorphic origin. This plateau is triangular in shape, having a broad base in the north and tapering towards Kanniyakumari in the south. The plateau extends from the Aravalli Range in the west up to the Chota Nagpur Plateau in the east. The Peninsular Plateau is divided by the rise Narmada into two parts:

The Malwa Plateau · The Deccan Plate

##### Quick Facts

The Himalayas are relatively young mountains formed from the sediment deposited in the ancient Tethys Sea. The Tethys Sea lay between ancient land masses of Laurasia in the north and Gondwanaland in the south about 185 million years ago. The two land masses moved closer due to movements inside the earth and then collided with each other. This caused the seabed of the Tethys Sea to fold upwards, forming the mountains. The Himalayas are rising even now.

They are fewer in number in the Andaman and Nicobar Islands. Many them are uninhabited. These islands form the smallest union territory of India.

#### Knowledge of India

It is difficult to believe that the Thar Desert was full of greenery in the past. Geological and historical evidence suggests that the Thar Desert had a very different climate and physical features in ancient times. Fateoclimate studies and fossil records indicate that the region was once covered by extensive grasslands and had a variety of flora and fauna. The presence of ancient riverbeds, lakes, and fossils of prehistoric animals further indicate the existence of a different environment that supported the growth of plants.

Over the course of thousands of years, climatic changes and human activities have gradually transformed the Thar Desert into a desert. Changes in rainfall patterns and the impact of human settlements and agricultural practices have caused the desertification of the region.

India has many large rivers. The Great Northern Plains have been built by the three major rivers of northern India—the Indus, the Ganga and the Brahmaputra. On the basis of the area of origin, rivers of India may be divided into two categories—the north Indian rivers or Himalayan rivers and the south Indian rivers or peninsular rivers.

## The North Indian Rivers or the Himalayan Rivers

The three important rivers—the Ganga, the Indus and the Brahmaputra originate in the snow-capped Himalayas. Each of these rivers with its tributaries and sub-tributaries, forms a distinct river system.

The river Indus, which is 2,900 km long, rises in Tibet. About 709 km of its length lies in India in the union territory of Jammu and Kashmir, from where it enters Pakistan and finally drains into the Arabian Sea, close to Karachi. The Satன, the Beas, the Ravi, the Chenab and the Jhelum are the five main tributaries of the Indus (Panchnadi).

The river Ganga, which is about 2,510 km long, flows through four states of India—Uttarakhand, Uttar Pradesh, Bihar and West Bengal. Its total basin area is approximately

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//ab1baae1-3869-4325-91f3-27d07130fe5c/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_526_1160_1026_1520.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2F1bf1618d8d7e7b811b3f708d266662a6a879108a6325170a8bf448a91cf567cc" alt="Image" width="42%" /></div>


The Ganga in the Himalayan mountains.

Uttarakhand

one-fourth of India's total area. The river Ganga, with its source in the Gangoti Glacier, is joined by many tributaries. Its left bank tributaries rise from the glaciers in the Himalayas. The Ramganga, the Gomti, the Ghaghara, the Gandak and the Kosi are the main left bank tributaries. The right bank tributaries rise from the peninsular region of the south. The Chambal, the Betwa and the Son are its major right bank tributaries. Only one right bank tributary, the Yamuna, rises from the Yamunotri Glacier in the Himalayas.

The river Brahmaputra, 2,700 km in length, rises near the Mansarovar Lake and flows eastwards through Tibet as the Tsang Po before entering India in Arunachal Pradesh. Some of the important tributaries of the river Brahmaputra are the Tista, the Barali, the Torsa and the Subansiri, which join it on the right bank. The Buri-Dihing, the Disang, the Kopilli, and the Dhansiri join it on its left bank. River Brahmaputra's upper course lies in Assam and in its lower course, it enters Bangladesh and joins the river Ganga. Both flow into the Bay of Bengal after building a fertile delta.

### The South Indian Rivers or the Peninsular Rivers

The leading rivers of south India are the Mahanadi, the Godavari, the Krishna, the Kaveri, the Narmada and the Tapi. These have been further classified as west-flowing and east-flowing rivers.

##### The West-flowing Rivers

These rivers drain into the Arabian Sea. They are short, swift-flowing rivers that rise in the Western Ghats. The two most important rivers are the Narmada and the Tapi.

system. It rises near the Amarkantak Plateau and flows between the Vindhyan and Satpura ranges before emptying itself into the Gulf of Khambhat near Bharuch in Gujarat. The Tapi (724 km) rises in the hills of Madhya Pradesh, flows south of the Satpura Range and drains into the Arabian Sea near Surat.

The Narmada is the longest (1,312 km) among the west-flowing rivers of the peninsular river The two rivers, the Narmada and the Tapi do not form deltas. The Narmada flows in a narrow rift valley between the Vindhyas and the Satpuras.

##### The East-flowing Rivers

These rivers flow towards the east and south east and drain into the Bay of Bengal.

The Godavari (1,465 km) is the longest river of the peninsular plateau of India. It is called 'the Ganga of the South'. It rises in Nashik distric and flows through the states of Maharashtra and Andhra Pradesh before draining into the Bay of Bengal.

The Mahanadi (851 km) rises in Madhya Pradesh, flows through Odisha and the enters the Bay of Bengal. It has a delta at its mouth.

##### Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs)

Goal 6: Clean Water and Sanitation

Goal 14: Life below Water

The Namami Gange Programme is an Integrated Conservation Mission launched by the Government of India in 2014. It seeks to achieve the reduction of pollution in the river Ganga and work towards its conservation and rejuvenation. A long-term goal for Ganga rejuvenation is to restore the endangered biodiversity of the river. Areas with high biodiversity have been identified for targeted conservation action.

##### Values and Life Skills

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//45cdeb70-e6c2-408e-8c69-e000edfaea82/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_49_939_113_1017.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2Fa0cccf037f34ed6efef3b942a82bb7297e05ff80203fd9a7f446e31c4a3b9394" alt="Image" width="5%" /></div>


Rivers have always been important to humans. They benefit communities in ways that are easily recognizable: they are a source of water for domestic, agricultural and industrial purposes and a large number of people earn their livelihood from the rivers. They are also a source of transportation and are often used for recreational and religious activities. So, we must keep the rivers clean and should not pollute them.

Do you think that pollution is increasing in rivers, streams and other water bodies? If yes, how can you help keep rivers and other water bodies clean and pollutant-free?

#### Biography

St George Everest (1790-1866 CE) was a British surveyor and geographer. He was the first Surveyor General of India and completed the Great Trigonometric Survey, surveying the meridian arc from the southernmost point of India north to Nepal (an area of more than 2400 kms). The world's highest peak, which had been called Peak XV, was renamed Mount Everest in his honour in 1865.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//45cdeb70-e6c2-408e-8c69-e000edfaea82/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_884_1372_1094_1589.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2Fd443fd1700b7614864e345e9c38bca5e8d0b0ed0e8d03b3939976c80038aee34" alt="Image" width="17%" /></div>

#### Important Terms

Pass: A gap through a mountain range that provides a route for travelling through it

Tributaries: Rivers that flow into a larger river, thereby contributing water to it

Alluvial plain: A plain formed by the sedimentary deposits of a river

#### Let's Do Something

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//45cdeb70-e6c2-408e-8c69-e000edfaea82/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_1099_1053_1160_1121.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F9104aa8d8760799a09d494715b0dd389cb30c358ca8d4e2f1f50dfb9d27f938d" alt="Image" width="5%" /></div>


A. Project work: Make a model of one of the physical features of India using materials such as clay, paper, cardboard and fabric. You can create mountains, deserts, islands, etc. Use toothpicks to make small flags with labels/names and have fun designing it.

TP B. Map work: With the help of your atlas, mark all the major Indian rivers on an outline map of India. Find the names of the cities that are on the banks of these rivers and mark them on the map.

TP C. Quiz: A fun quiz can be organized in class to locate places and physical features on a wall map of India.

# Aryabhata

Anyabhatu (476-550 c.f.) was a renowned astronomer, mathematician and scientist in ancient India. He is known for his path-breaking discoveries and theories. He is said to be the founder of 'zero'. He developed the approximate value of pi (pi) and contributed to trigonometry.

The Sanskrit term for geography is Bhugol shastra or bhushastra. Bhug means earth and gol means round. It is said that the term bhugal was for the first time mentioned in the book Surya Siddhanto written by Aryabhata, around 500 c.

In his book the Surya Siddhanta, Anyabhata gave much geographical knowledge to us, such as the spherical shape of the earth, the calculation of Nugas (geological time), eclipses etc.

From the term, it is clear that in ancient India, it was common knowledge that the earth is round, and nut flat.

MOON

Dark shadow

Light shadow

Also, it was Aryabhata who had said that the earth rotates on its axis, which is the cause of day and night.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e3243ddc-4e3f-403b-9b65-02126fc4b73f/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_40_0_711_688.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2Fb7ebb1395bd210da6c684786c44c4e5c8f99df8c37022e606a8889979d35de11" alt="Image" width="56%" /></div>


If we go by the modern estimates, Aryabhata has found the circumference almost accurately less than 1 per cent. was 39,968 km, which is off the current value of by just 0.27 per cent. He achieved this less at the there were no accurate time-scoping devices at a unit of measurement.

Equator

The two locations that were identified by Anyabhata, possibly, one of them was Ujjain, because he believed that it was situated at the Tropic of Cancer. The one he mentioned was Khandwa, the city in Madhya Pradesh.

Anyabhata perhaps identified two different locations A and B on the same latitude. He then proceeded to calculate the distance between A, B, and B, and the time difference between the two using the mood's position or a water clock. He used the information to calculate the circumference of the latitudeal circle. From this, he would have calculated the equatorial circumference using the linear-ōth-ōth-ōth-ōth-ōth distance.

Aryabhata contributed significantly to Indian science, astronomy, mathematics and geography. The Government of India named the first artificial satellite of India 'Aryabhata' in his honour. It was launched in 1975.

10

# India—Climate, Flora and Fauna

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e3243ddc-4e3f-403b-9b65-02126fc4b73f/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_25_378_83_476.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A30Z%2F-1%2F%2Fdb5317aeb975542c387f608e0bdf7caf99881b1401c067d01adf0bf6ed27becf" alt="Image" width="4%" /></div>


### Learning Outcomes

#### The learner:

compares the relief, climate and vegetation of India with other parts of Asia.

discusses the importance of monsoon and its impact on the socio-cultural unity of India.

#### Recall

##### Stilli: Analysing

The Tropic of Cancer passes through India.

Would the climate of India be different if the Equator was passing through it? Why or why not?

In the previous chapter, you learnt about the political divisions and physical features of India. Let us now take a look at how these determine the climate and vegetation of India.

#### CLIMATE

India is a large country with a great variety of physical features. The Tropic of Cancer, at  $ 23\frac{1}{2} $°N latitude, divides India into two nearly equal parts—the northern temperate zone and the southern tropical zone. The climatic conditions also, therefore, vary from place to place.

The areas away from the coast experience extremes of temperature while those near the coast have equable climate throughout the year. The southern part of India lies near the equator and is, therefore, warm all year round. But areas in the extreme north, such as Jammu and Kashmir, experience low temperatures and snowfall in winter.

Despite these differences, India is said to

have a tropical monsoon climate, which means that the temperatures here are higher than those in the temperate latitudes. This happens because of the Himalayas, which do not allow the cold winds of Asia to reach the temperate northern parts of India, and trap the monsoons—the seasonal winds that bring rain to the whole of India. Economic activities, such as agriculture, forestry and fishing in different parts of India are influenced directly by the amount of rainfall. The climate also has a direct influence on industry, trade and tourism.

#### Factors Affecting the Climate of India

##### Latitude

The Tropic of Cancer passes through the middle of India, because of this the southern part lies in the tropical zone and the northern part in the temperate zone.

The southern part of the country has equable climate—neither very hot nor very cold—as it is close to the equator. The northern part, which is far from the equator, is hot in summer and cold in winter.

##### Height above sea level

Very low temperatures are recorded in the high Himalayan regions and even in

places such as Udhagamandalam (Ooty) and Kodaikanal in the Western Ghats. This is because temperature decreases with an increase in height above sea level.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e3243ddc-4e3f-403b-9b65-02126fc4b73f/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_168_270_259_342.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F1b270b5e332c909b12716c0b4c39b9add3cf10e9d52b36d3843ebdb84dac7e61" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>


##### Did You Know?

Hottest place in India: Phalodi in Rajasthan (51°C); Coldest place in India: Dras in Ladakh (~45°C); Wettest place in India: Mawsynram in Meghalaya (average annual rainfall 1,187 cm)

##### Northern mountains

The Northern Mountains prevent the cold winds of Central Asia from entering India. They prevent India from experiencing very cold winters. The Himalayas also prevent the rain-bearing monsoon winds from leaving the country thus allowing the country to receive sufficient rainfall.

##### Distance from the sea

Places in the interior have extricate climate as they are far from the moderating influence of the sea. Thus, places such as Punjab, Haryana and Rajasthan have very hot summers and cold dry winters. However, places nearer the coasts, such as Mumbai and Chennai, have moderate summers and winters.

##### Seasons

The climate of India is characterized by the following four main seasons:

1. The Hot Dry Season or the Summer season---March to May

2. The Hot Wet Season or the Rainy season—June to October September

3. The Retreating Monsoons—October to November.

4. The Cool Dry Season on the Winter season—November/December to February

The hot dry season or the summer season

The temperature starts to rise by March. May, the highest temperatures are recorded in the desert regions of the north-west where the maximum temperatures may range above 48°C. This is the period when the sun direct rays move northwards towards the Tropic of Cancer. In the Northern Plains, the temperatures are about 35° to 40°C. However, the places at higher altitudes and the coast regions have moderate temperatures to their height above sea level and proximate to the sea respectively.

A low pressure area develops over the Northern plains and stretches from the Tdesert to the Chota Nagpur plateau.

The high temperature during this season leads to ascending air currents, causing local storms in some areas. At some places, these storms are accompanied by convectional showers. The storms have different local names and different places. In Rajasthan, the hot dust wind blowing from the desert is called the loo. In Kerala, local showers known as mango showers help in the ripening of mangoes.

In Assam and West Bengal, similar thunderstorms have been given the local name of kalbaisakhi, meaning 'calamity of the month of Baisakh' (April), as they sometimes damage trees and property.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e3243ddc-4e3f-403b-9b65-02126fc4b73f/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_710_1165_797_1245.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F4cc78faa8a7677dfd5eb3656c1c7031f7d88a74827f93c4ac3f34c8e906fcb4a" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>


##### Knowledge of India

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e3243ddc-4e3f-403b-9b65-02126fc4b73f/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_1079_1165_1186_1237.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F93466a56434d1139bcc75ee8b38579af05cf9bf47ba58031f2097a978210c1b6" alt="Image" width="8%" /></div>


Mango showers are a familiar term to describe the rain before the monsoon. These rains usually occur between the months of March and April, though their arrival is usually tough to predict. Their intensity can vary from light rains to heavy and persistent storms. As an advantage, the mango showers prepare soil for summer crops, replenish water reservoirs and provide relief from extreme heat.

##### The hot wet season of the farmy season

By June, the high temperature leads to the formation of a low pressure area over the north-western part of the continent. Due to the differential rate of heating of the land and water, the air above the surrounding seas and oceans is relatively cooler and creates a high pressure region over them. This air moves from the high pressure region to the low pressure region, i.e., from the sea to the land.

The winds blowing towards the land absorb moisture from the water bodies and bring rainfall to the land. These winds are called summer monsoons or the south-west monsoons that bring heavy downpours accompanied by thunder and lightning. They bring relief from the scorching heat. Temperatures decrease by 3°-6°C after the onset of the monsoons.

Kerala is the first state to receive the rain. Owing to the peninsular shape of India, the south-west monsoon winds are divided into two branches: the Arabian Sea branch and the Bay of Bengal branch.

#### The Arabian Sea branch

The Arabian Sea branch is stronger and causes heavy rainfall, as high as 250 cm, in the western part of the Western Ghats. Condensation is followed by sudden precipitation, associated with lightning and thunder. This is called the 'burst of monsoon.' Sometimes during the south west monsoon season, wet spells are followed by weak winds and dry weather. This is known as a 'break in the monsoons'. The Aravallis run parallel to the winds and so Rajasthan gets scanty rainfall. After crossing the Western Ghats, it advances over the Deccan Plateau and the interior of the southern peninsula hardly gets 50-60 cm of rainfall during the rainy season as it lies on the leeward side of the Western Ghats.

#### The Bay of Bengal branch

The Bay of Bengal branch brings heavy rainfall in north-eastern India. The monsoon wind is forced to take a turn towards the northwest, along the curve of the Himalayas, causing rainfall over the Northern Plains. The Himalayas block this branch from crossing over to China. When the monsoon reaches north-western India, the moisture is spent and the wind becomes dry. As a result rainfall is very low in this part of the country.

##### The retreating monsoons

By the end of September, with the sun's direct rays moving towards the equator and the Tropic of Capricorn, the Indian subcontinent starts to cool again. Since the air above the land is cold and heavy, a high pressure region is created over land. The air above the surrounding water bodies, on the other hand, is relatively warmer and creates regions of low pressure over them. Now, the winds reverse their direction and start blowing from the land to the sea, and the monsoon winds start withdrawing from India. These winds are called retreating monsoons. Tamil Nadu receives less rainfall in summer from the south-west monsoon as it lies on the leeward side of the Western Ghats. However, it receives more rainfall in winter from the north-east monsoon.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e3243ddc-4e3f-403b-9b65-02126fc4b73f/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_601_1133_704_1215.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2F34faa5e6e0af1b1d368901322f0ed7abce9699f785bf7d456adb2958a79ccdc7" alt="Image" width="8%" /></div>


#### Did You Know?

The arrival of the monsoons, changes in seasons, and the harvest season are all celebrated with festivals such as Adi Perukku and Pongal in Tamil Nadu, and Baisakhi in north India.

#### Cold dry season

The winter season begins to set in by November and lasts till February. Temperatures are

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//7de786d6-72d3-4f63-8b6f-2266f60b7ba3/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_101_53_755_887.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F1e7f433d8c87a6377756e06cb39d843db880ef6b4c29913e96d821beb2209acc" alt="Image" width="54%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">▲ India: Pressure, Temperature and Winds in January</div> </div>


lower in north India, and the interiors are dry. The average temperatures go below  $ 10^{\circ} $C in northwest India and are around  $ 21^{\circ} $C elsewhere in the plains. At high altitudes, the temperatures are very low. Some areas at higher altitudes such as Srinagar and Shimla experience snowfall. South India remains warmer owing to it being closer to the equator. Chennai remains pleasant at  $ 24^{\circ} $C. Cold waves—severe cold conditions—are common in northern India.

North-west India receives rains from depressions or cyclones originating in the Mediterranean region. They blow eastwards and enter India. They are known as western disturbances and bring cyclonic rainfall only to the north-western parts of India.

Punjab, Kashmir, Himachal Pradesh, and western Uttar Pradesh receive rainfall because of these depressions. Though the amount of rainfall is low, it is extremely important for the cultivation of rabies or winter crops such as wheat and barley.

Rainfall over the entire subcontinent during this season is scanty as there is a high-pressure system on the land, and the winds are blowing from the land mass towards the sea and hence are dry. But two areas do receive some rainfall in winter—the Coromandel Coast and northwest India. The winds that are blowing in this season from the north are deflected towards their right because of the Coriolis force and blow as north-east monsoons. They cause rainfall on the Coromandel Coast, which is why Tamil Nadu receives rainfall in winter.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//7de786d6-72d3-4f63-8b6f-2266f60b7ba3/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_668_934_759_1015.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2Fb887472fc16c15bb943574a036cef39a8e61dd9be0b95eae36ce25cb8c46c06a" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>


##### Think and Answer

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//7de786d6-72d3-4f63-8b6f-2266f60b7ba3/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_1128_913_1175_988.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F82d733d4aee50dfc2e61a4145f994beb4005b91705fe9b3371c7a913b987a16a" alt="Image" width="3%" /></div>


Skill: Critical Thinking

How do you think that economic activities, such as agriculture, forestry and fishing in different parts of India are influenced directly by the climate? C-6.4

##### Rainfall

Rainfall in India is related to the winds and the relief features of the land. The amount of rainfall depends on the location of a place, i.e., whether it is located near the coast or in the interior and whether it is on the windward side or the leeward side. The direction of the mountain ranges is also of great significance. The moisture-laden south-west monsoon winds from the Arabian Sea branch cause

Tamil Nadu receives little rainfall in summer from the south-west monsoon as it lies in the rain-shadow region of the Western Ghats. It receives most rainfall in winter from the northeast monsoon.

Other economic activities like forestry and fishing are also influenced directly by the amount of rainfall.

- Monsoon rain gives us respite from the high and intolerable summer heat and brings back life to the living earth.

• Monsoon also has a role to play in the socio-cultural unity of India. People of India, particularly the farmers, eagerly wait for the monsoon rains. We know that the monsoon winds provide water for the various agricultural activities. The agricultural calendar, and the social-cultural life of the people including their festivities, revolve around the monsoon phenomena and in a way binds the people of India together.

Excess of monsoon causes flood which damage life and property and destroys crops. #### VEGETATION

We have just learnt that the relief features and climate vary in the different parts of our country. Consequently, there is a great variety of vegetation and forest types in India. There are about 5,000 different species of plants and trees found in India. Vegetation in India can be divided into the following types:

• Tropical evergreen forests

• Tropical deciduous forests

• Desert forests/Thorn forest/scrub

U. Based on variation of relief:

• Tidal forests

• Mountain forests

#### Tropical Evergreen Rainforests

These forests are found in areas that receive an annual rainfall of over 300 cm and are very humid.

The temperature varies between  $ 25^{\circ} $ and  $ 27^{\circ} $C or above.

The forests have broad-leaved hardwood trees. These are dense evergreen forests which have trees growing up to 60 m.

Tropical evergreen rainforest

The trees form distinct layers. Thick undergrowth makes commercial exploitation difficult. Shisham, ebony, rosewood, telsar, tun or red cedar, teak gurjan, mahogany and bamboo are the common species of trees growing here.

The windward side of the Western Ghats in western Maharashtra, Kerala and Karnataka, the hills of north-eastern India and the Andaman and Nicobar Islands have these forests.

The forests are found in a large area—from the eastern slopes of the Western Ghats up to the Shiwalik Range in the north. They are also found in the north-eastern region and the Deccan Plateau.

The trees are deciduous trees, which shed their leaves during the dry season to conserve water. The trees are shorter than those found in the tropical evergreen forests. They do not grow too close to each other. They have long roots.
