1. Why is Rajasthan a desert?

2. Why does the amount of rainfall caused by the south-west monsoon decrease as we move to the north-west across the Ganga plain? C-6.1

#### VEGETATION

We have just learnt that the relief features and climate vary in the different parts of our country. Consequently, there is a great variety of vegetation and forest types in India. There are about 5,000 different species of plants and trees found in India. Vegetation in India can be divided into the following types:

I. Based on variation of rainfall:

• Tropical evergreen forests

• Tropical deciduous forests

• Desert forests/Thorn forest/scrub

II. Based on variation of relief:

Tidal forests

• Mountain forests

#### Tropical Evergreen Rainforests

These forests are found in areas that receive an annual rainfall of over 300 cm and are very humid.

- The temperature varies between  $ 25^{\circ} $ and  $ 27^{\circ} $C or above.

The forests have broad-leaved hardwood trees. These are dense evergreen forests which have trees growing up to 60 m.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//7de786d6-72d3-4f63-8b6f-2266f60b7ba3/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_573_197_1125_471.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A30Z%2F-1%2F%2Fe9d244b5125f268b99de207ba95f03e1b969fba17c6ec6af63412ef16c9dc765" alt="Image" width="46%" /></div>


▲ Tropical evergreen rainforest

The trees form distinct layers. Thick undergrowth makes commercial exploitation difficult. Shisham, ebony, rosewood, telsar, tun or red cedar, teak gurjan, mahogany and bamboo are the common species of trees growing here.

The windward side of the Western Ghats in western Maharashtra, Kerala and Karnataka, the hills of north-eastern India and the Andaman and Nicobar Islands have the most forests.

##### Monsoon Deciduous Forests

These forests are found in areas that receive an annual rainfall between 100 and 200 cm, have distinct dry and wet seasons and a low range of temperature.

The forests are found in a large area—from the eastern slopes of the Western Ghats up to the Shiwalik Range in the north. They are also found in the north-eastern region and the Deccan Plateau.

The trees are deciduous trees, which shed their leaves during the dry season to conserve water. The trees are shorter than those found in the tropical evergreen forests. They do not grow too close to each other. They have long roots.

The trees growing here are of great economic importance. Teak, sal, mahua, khair, sandalwood, jackfruit, semal, myrobalan and banyan are the main species of trees growing here.

##### Thorn and Desert Forests

These forests are found in the north-western part of India and on the leeward side of the Western Ghats. Large parts of Rajasthan, Punjab, and Haryana and some parts of Madhya Pradesh, Maharashtra, Andhra Pradesh, and Gujarat have these forests.

The average rainfall is less than 50 cm.

The vegetation cover is not dense. Stunted, thorny trees and bushes grow here. The plants have long roots to tap the underground water and modified stems to store water. Date palms, acacia, palas, cachi, kikar and babool are the dominant trees.

#### Tidal or Mangrove Forests

These forests are found in the deltas of a major rivers—the Ganga-Brahmaputra Delta (the Sundarbans), and the deltas of the Mahanadi, the Godavari, the Krishna and the Kaveri. These areas receive more than 200 cm of annual rainfall.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//2950d1bf-a58a-4880-b07b-f3f6b82f1895/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_263_585_1092_1490.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2F41357e99ebe8c6b10d01e2a1167485a859172ddba2f7620ea7ea683b3a8f9b4d" alt="Image" width="69%" /></div>


India: Natural Vegetation

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//2950d1bf-a58a-4880-b07b-f3f6b82f1895/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_29_78_541_408.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2Fd9ac1e19bd9f3346f2b63397ea9372caaddf373f6af0f2eabe9345da521662f9" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>


Mangrove forests are a very important part of the coastal ecosystem.

The forests have developed in lowlands, the lands that get flooded and submerged under salty sea waters during high tides. The forests are dense and the trees have hardwood.

The trees have stilt-like supporting roots that can take in oxygen. They have glossy and evergreen leaves. Sundari trees, gorjan, lintal, casuarina, golpata, hogla (elephant grass), hetal and reeds are mainly found here. These forests are also called mangroves.

##### Mountain or Alpine Forests

These forests are mainly found in the Himalayas in Jammu and Kashmir, Himachal Pradesh, Uttarakhand, and Arunachal Pradesh.

Belts of different types of vegetation occur at different altitudes. The lower foothills have deciduous forests and the middle slopes have mixed deciduous conifers.

Grass grows on very high slopes. Coniferous forests have softwood evergreen trees. Sal, oak, ash, beech, chir pine, silver fir, chestnut, cedar and deodar are the common species of trees growing here.

#### WILDLIFE

A great variety of animals are found in different parts of the country. The tiger, the largest animal of the cat family is the national animal of India. The Royal Bengal tiger is mainly found in the Sunderbans of the Ganga Delta, and in the forests and the foothills of the Himalayas.

The Asiatic lion, the king of beasts, is found in only one part of India—the Gir forests of Gujarat. Panthers, cheetahs, and rare snow leopards are other wild cats found in India.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//2950d1bf-a58a-4880-b07b-f3f6b82f1895/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_564_440_1107_745.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F167b8b555d8c003704918b68766fa88090e8c219992450987720d27d98240c83" alt="Image" width="45%" /></div>


The Asiatic lion

However, their numbers have greatly decreased in recent years due to indiscriminate hunting and cutting down of forests.

Elephants are mainly found in the southern states of Karnataka, Tamil Nadu, Kerala, and the north-eastern states.

The Nilgai or the blue bull is mainly found in areas north of the river Godavari. The swamp deer of Assam, the barasingha of Madhya Pradesh, and the hangul of Kashmir form a group of deer that have twelve tips on their horns. Bears are found in many forest areas. The snow-covered mountains of the Himalayas are the natural habitat of the red panda and the Himalayan black bear. The one-horned rhinoceros found in Assam and West Bengal has recently been introduced in Uttar Pradesh.

Of the reptile family, crocodiles abound in different parts of the country. Among them the gharial or Gangetic crocodile is found

only in Odisha, Assam, and Uttar Pradesh along the large rivers. The saltwater crocodile is confined to the Sunderbans in West Bengal, Odisha, and the Andaman and Nicobar Islands.

Birds such as the swallow, mynah, owl, kite, parrot, pigeon, dove, crow, sparrow and bulbul are common in India. The peacock is the national bird of India.

## IMPORTANCE OF FORESTS AND WILDLIFE

The total forest area (percentage of land area) in India was last reported at 21.34 per cent in 2015, according to data provided by the Indian State of Forest Report 2015. The National Forest Policy of India states that at least one-third or 33 per cent of the land area of India should be under forest. However, at present, India falls short of its goal by a little more than 10 per cent. This data also reflects India's fast-reducing forest cover, and at the same time emphasizes the need for the conservation of our forests and wildlife. This is important because forests not only provide food and shelter to different kinds of animals; forests are also the source of livelihood for about 10 lakh people in India. All of us derive some direct and indirect uses from forests.

##### Direct Uses

Forests provide timber for construction purposes, furniture, toys, railway sleepers, sports goods and wood carving and softwood, bamboo, and grass for pulp, paper and plywood.

• Forests also provide products such as fruits, flowers, medicinal herbs and plants, beeswax, honey, turpentine, oil, lac and resin.

• Forests are a wildlife.

• Forests provide fodder for cattle.

#### Indirect Uses

Forests are major tourist attractions.

Forests moderate the temperature of place.

Forests protect land from soil erosion by reducing the flow of floodwaters.

Forests help in increasing soil fertility by providing humus.

Forests help in increasing water vapour in the atmosphere, thereby helping in cloud formation that causes rainfall.

#### CONSERVATION

To protect India's forests and wildlife, the government has converted much of India's forest cover into protected zones by setting up national parks, sanctuaries and biosphere reserves. Felling of trees and clearing off forest cover is either prohibited in these regions, or restricted.

A sanctuary is a protected area where wild animals can live in their natural surroundings. Hunting, entry with weapons, lighting a fire and using substances injurious to wildlife are prohibited, while fishing and grazing of livestock may be allowed on a controlled basis. Permission to enter or reside in a sanctuary may be granted by the Chief Wildlife Warden for purposes of photography, scientific research or tourism.

A national park is similar to a sanctuary except that cattle grazing is prohibited. In addition, exploitation or removal of any wildlife, or its habitat, is prohibited within a national park.

Biosphere reserves are also protected areas that have been set up to preserve genetic diversity, promote research on ecological conservation, and facilitate training to create an awareness of the biosphere.

At present, there are about 514 wildlife sanctuaries and 100 national parks in different parts of our country.

### Effort towards Afforestation

A tree planting ceremony called Vana Mahotsava was started in India to maintain the ecological balance and prevent the depletion of the ozone layer. The following activities are undertaken on Vana Mahotsava:

Tree planting to increase area under forests

Care of trees already planted

Protection of trees from insects and pests

. planting trees on hill slopes and wastelands

Preventing illegal felling of trees

. Free distribution of saplings

#### National Parks in India

India's national parks play an important role in conserving the country's forests and wildlife. Some of the well-known national parks are mentioned below:

- Kaziranga National Park: It is located in Assam and gives protection to the one horned-rhinoceros.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//2950d1bf-a58a-4880-b07b-f3f6b82f1895/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_22_979_543_1293.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A30Z%2F-1%2F%2Fea64596062fa567c3b4c58151e2c21cd6c0c0f3b618964c66176e82952224390" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>


##### One-homed rhinoceros

Ranthambore National Park: Located in Sawai Madhopur district of Rajasthan, this park is dotted with banyan, dhok and mango trees and also has evergreen belts. It plays an important role in tiger protection in the country.

Sundarbans National Park: It is located in West Bengal and is a major tiger reserve in the country.

Randhavgarh National Park: Located in Madhya Pradesh, this park is another safe haven for tigers.

- Kanha National Park: It is supposed to be the most well-maintained park in the country. It provided inspiration to Rudyard Kipling for his famous work, 'The Jungle Book.

- Corbett National Park: It is located in the foothills of the Himalayas and is known for its natural scenic beauty. It has been named after Jim Corbett, a famous hunter-turned-conservationist. This park is well known for its tiger reserve.

• Gir National Park: It is located in Gujarat and is famous for the Asiatic lion.

Keoladeo Ghana National Park: It is located at Bharatpur in Rajasthan and was formerly known as Bharatpur Bird Sanctuary.

Periyar National park: It is located in Kerala and is noted for both elephant and tiger reserves.

##### Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs)

##### Goal 15: Life on land

The National Tiger Conservation Authority (NTCA) has worked towards tiger conservation in India. It uses on-the-ground protection initiatives and also monitors tigers and their habitats through latest technology.

##### Wildlife Sanctuaries of India

There are different varieties of animal and plant life found in the wildlife sanctuaries of India. Some examples of wildlife sanctuaries are given below:

Kachchh Desert Wildlife Sanctuary: It is situated in the Great Rann of Kachchh in the Kachchh district of Gujarat. This

sanctuary encompasses a true saline desert where thousands of flamingoes nest and breed in the world-famous 'Flamingo City'. It is home to many resident and migratory birds, including raptors and Houbara bustard.

Wild Ass Sanctuary: It encompasses a large area of Little Rann of Kachchh and the and nearby districts in the state of Gujarat. It is world famous for its wild as population.

Anamalai Wildlife Sanctuary: It is located

Chilika Wildlife Sanctuary: It is located in Odisha and is home to various migratory and local birds such as flamingo, bar-headed goose, spot-billed pelican, spoonbill, white-bellied sea eagle, brahminy kite, open-billed stork, ibis, kingfisher, heron, egret, gull, tern, etc.

It is home to hundreds of species of resident birds, which stay here all year around. The number increases in winters, when there is an influx of birds from the Central Asia region.

##### Did You Know?

The World Wildlife Fund, India, was established in 1969. In 1986 it became World Wide Fund for Nature—India. It has several offices in different states of India such as Andhra Pradesh, Himachal Pradesh, Odisha, and Tamil Nadu.

##### Biosphere Reserves in India

national parks and/or reserves that are open to some economic uses. In these reserves, protection is given not only to the flora and fauna of the region but also to the local communities and their way of life. Biosphere reserves are divided into three zones which have specific roles to play in the conservation of wildlife.

India biosphere reserves are large areas of natural habitat and often include one or two

Core zone is the legally protected zone wherein land and water is not to be disturbed by human activity. The main function of this zone is to conserve biodiversity and allow scientific research that does not adversely affect the wildlife in the zone. Buffer zone is the area surrounding the core zone wherein activities like environmental research and recreation are allowed in a manner that does not affect the wildlife. Transition zone is the area wherein human activities such as farming, grazing and any other activities of the indigenous people are permitted.

Some important biosphere reserves in India are

- Nilgiri Biosphere Reserve, located in Western Ghats and Nilgiri Hills in South India

- Gulf of Mannar Biosphere Reserve, located between India and Sri Lanka, forming part of the Laccadive Sea

- Sundarbans Biosphere Reserve in West Bengal

Nanda Devi Biosphere in north-eastern Uttarakhand

Nokrek Biosphere Reserve in the West Garo Hills in Meghalaya

Pachmari Biosphere Reserve in the Satpura Range in Madhya Pradesh

· Similipal Biosphere Reserve in north-eastern Odisha

• Achanakmar-Amarkantak Biosphere Reserve located in Chhattisgarh and Madhya Pradesh

Great Nicobar Biosphere Reserve located in Nicobar Islands

#### Biography

Dev Raj Sikka (1934–2017) was a renowned meteorologist who became known for his studies on the Indian monsoon, getting him the title 'Monsoon Man'. He was the first to highlight the connection between the El Nino phenomenon and the Indian monsoon. For 40 years, Sikka carried out research and promotion of atmospheric and oceanic sciences across the country.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d96b89e5-a032-498e-976e-ab722ee562c1/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_989_379_1177_593.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A30Z%2F-1%2F%2F7cf5f103c1a47298119f282a9cc24ece7e405be972be6308304b4e4cccb27530" alt="Image" width="15%" /></div>

##### Important Terms

Too: Hot and dusty wind blowing over northern India

Tropical monsoon climate: A climate characterized by distinct wet and dry seasons

Monsoons: Seasonal winds blowing across the Indian subcontinent

Western disturbances: Cyclones originating in the Mediterranean region and arriving into India from the north-west

Gross domestic product: The total value of all the goods and services produced by a country in one year

Evergreen Forest: A forest that remains green throughout the year, that is, the trees of the forest do not shed their leaves in any season

Deciduous Forest: Tree a tree that sheds its leaves in the dry season

Mangrove Forest: A forest that is found in the tropical and sub-tropical coastal areas

which are subject to being submerged by high tides

# 11 Human Resources in India

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d9657231-3f4b-4059-bf0a-009e0ca5a399/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_135_304_224_397.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F3bd33dff68dc28abffda6851721f71216d7bd7b07abc7fe00c2aa12b270eb2bc" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>


##### Learning Outcomes

The learner:

> discusses the meaning of human resource.

 $ ^{*} $ describes the role of health and education in developing human resources.

understands the meaning of skilled and unskilled human resource.

identifies areas in India lagging behind in development due to unavailability of unskilled human resource.

» analyses factors responsible for development of any area.

##### Recall

##### Skill: Analysing

Sahil was looking at the population map of India.

He noticed that the plains have a significantly larger population than other areas. Why is it so? C-6.4

A resource is something that a country, an organization or an individual can use, especially to increase their wealth. Human beings are also a resource as they can help a country meet its needs and help in its economic growth. In fact, human beings are the most important resource of a country because they can use their intelligence and ability to exploit other resources such as land, minerals and water in the best possible way.

#### MEANING OF HUMAN RESOURCES

Human resources refer to the entire population of a country along with its knowledge, skill, abilities, efficiency, far-sightedness, technical knowledge and physical and mental capacity to do work. In order to attain economic development, proper utilization of both natural as well as human resources is important. Since human beings are the vital instruments of production, the progress of a country depends on the quality and efficiency of its people. Therefore, a country should focus on manpower planning for the development of its human resources and on improving their living conditions.

## SKILLED AND UNSKILLED HUMAN RESOURCES

The working population of a country can be divided into skilled and unskilled human resources.

##### Skilled Human Resources

• A skilled person is someone who has specialized training to perform their work.

- These people have different levels of formal education.

• Scientists, doctors, engineers, teachers, IT professionals, lawyers, etc., are examples of skilled human resource.

- These people perform tasks that require knowledge and skill, and they cannot be easily replaced.

• They generally earn a high income.

### Unskilled Human Resources

Unskilled human resource includes people with little formal education and very limited skills.

Workers at construction sites, sanitation workers, domestic helps, etc., are examples of unskilled human resource.

Their jobs do not require any specialized skill and these people can easily be replaced.

They generally earn a low wage.

### Impact of Skilled Human Resource on the Socio-economic Development

Human resources play an important role in the overall development of a country.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d9657231-3f4b-4059-bf0a-009e0ca5a399/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_13_727_522_1076.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2Fa0d18c6900034f4c434971427cfd43a4cb908b8bca3cab150e22e59dddef223a" alt="Image" width="42%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">Construction professionals</div> </div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d9657231-3f4b-4059-bf0a-009e0ca5a399/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_14_1119_528_1421.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2Faeea52c83af0e82f46961916f32a87577e20a65f4e4bc93dec4cf04760936afc" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>


Human resources are required for the proper utilization of a country's natural resources

An IT worker

like mineral, water, forest, etc., because the optimal utilization of these resources is necessary for the economic development of the country. Countries such as Japan, Hong Kong, Singapore, etc. which are poor in natural resources have been able to achieve high economic growth by properly utilizing their human resources. Factories and industries can run only if we have trained people to operate machinery and equipment.

Skilled and the knowledgeable human resources make a rational use of all resources at their disposal and increase the volume of output and income for a country. They are well versed in using modern technology and thus help to bring development in a country. They help to increase production by producing a variety of goods and services of high quality. Therefore, the government must invest substantially in acquiring and increasing the number of persons who have skills, education and experience, which are crucial for the economic and political development of the country.

The development of human resource works as a tool for economic change. It can make people knowledgeable, skilled and physically healthy. This can lead to a change in the attitudes of the people, develop their thought process and improve the quality of their life. Such changes encourage the spirit of entrepreneurship and motivate people to work hard, take risks, do research and explore their innovative capacity. All these things help people develop new processes of production and create new products.

The population of a country is its biggest asset. In order to develop its human resources and effectively utilize the potential and ability of its people for the development and progress of the country, the government needs to invest substantially in its people.

First of all, the government should ensure that people get balanced food to stay healthy and physically fit. Improved health facility and medical care can enhance the physical capacity of people. If people are healthy, they will be able to work hard and increase their productivity.

People should be literate and education of different kinds—elementary, technical, vocational and professional—should be provided to them. Education with proper skill-based training enhances people's employment opportunities for people. Attainment of vocational skills helps all categories of workers to earn high income in different professions. Education and training at higher educational levels like college and universities with specialized skill training in technical, engineering, accounting, management, and other such courses help people to contribute significantly towards increased productivity.

People should be trained in the latest production technologies. Their technological knowledge and skills should be updated. This improved knowledge will increase the productive capacity of a country. A country should also encourage people to go abroad and get trained in latest technologies. This will encourage transfer of technology from foreign countries to one's own country. This will enable a country to introduce modern technology into its production, which in turn, can improve its productive capacities and eventually lead to higher growth of the economy.

People in many developing countries do not have the required skills and knowledge necessary for its industrial sector. These

Increased investment in human resource development can raise the per capita income of the country. Imparting requisite knowledge and training to the workforce in specific areas can improve the productivity of workers and therefore, raise the per capita income.

## ROLE OF HEALTH AND EDUCATION IN DEVELOPING HUMAN RESOURCES

Health and education play a very important role in the development of human resource.

- Healthy people can work well and do things quickly.

They are also able to utilize other resources in a better way. You must have experienced that when you fall ill you are not able to study properly and prepare well for your exams.

Also, when people spend money treatment, they lose this valuable resource which they can use to acquire other valuable resources or enhance their skills.

Education too is an important factor for the development of human resource.

- When a person receives good education, it improves his or her level of understanding.

It also increases their capacity and mental efficiency to produce more.

More importantly, good education changes the attitude and behaviour of people as they gain more confidence in themselves.

A country with a high proportion of well-educated people can, therefore, achieve rapid economic growth.

## Impact of Skilled Human Resource on the Socio-economic Development of India

Education is essential for the socio-economic development of a country and plays a key role in the development of skilled human resources. Studies have shown that investing in educational skills promotes economic growth in a country. The Indian government has invested heavily in human resource development because it sees a return on this investment in the form of economic growth. But education alone is not sufficient. For proper utilization of human resources, skill learning is necessary.

In India, skill training has not received the attention it deserves except perhaps for limited professions like engineers, doctors and certain types of technical experts like computer professionals.

The government has started the 'Skill India Mission' for the youth in order to meet the demands for skilled workers and for the economic growth of the nation.

Through this mission the unemployed, school dropouts, women, ordinary graduates, etc. are given training based on their knowledge and ability which will prepare them for jobs.

Training is also to be given to carpenters, masons, blacksmiths, cobblers, welders, tailors, weavers, etc.

### DISTRIBUTION OF POPULATION IN INDIA

India is the most populous country in the world. We have just 2.4 per cent of the land area of the world but have about 17 per cent of the world's population. Our population is more than the population of North America, South America and Australia put together.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d9657231-3f4b-4059-bf0a-009e0ca5a399/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_546_386_639_466.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A30Z%2F-1%2F%2Ffd2f21bd175bedfd9a82b421e9cf74a2ffec2a7e9150f399d2e90afe76abeec4" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>


#### Did You Know?

The census (counting of the country's population) is conducted every 10 years in India.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d9657231-3f4b-4059-bf0a-009e0ca5a399/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_555_577_618_648.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A30Z%2F-1%2F%2F08868e794af8df3a427f9021272df216ac4d28db1f1c46d72b362e25eb4956d8" alt="Image" width="5%" /></div>


##### Quick Facts

The Human Development Index (HDI), devised by the United Nations Development Programme (UNDP), measures the level of development in a country. This index is calculated on the basis of per capita income, education, literacy and life expectancy of the population.

According to the Human Development Report 2021-22, India's rank on the Human Development Index (HDI) has gone down from 130 in 2020 to 132 in 2022, due the setback during the Covid-19 pandemic.

##### Rural-Urban Composition

Population of India may be classified into rural and urban depending on where people live. The population living in the village is termed rural and the population living in cities and towns is termed as urban. Rural and urban people differ from each other in their way of life, their jobs, their customs and traditions and attitudes. Rural people generally earn their livelihood from agriculture, livestock rearing and other allied activities. Urban people, on the other hand, earn their livelihood from jobs in offices, factories, trade, transport and services.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d9657231-3f4b-4059-bf0a-009e0ca5a399/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_129_81_773_888.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F680358b7e2235e2d9eab6fe2e6b55460a2244802d8ea3489da84ecb7c71e06ae" alt="Image" width="54%" /></div>

##### Knowledge of India

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d9657231-3f4b-4059-bf0a-009e0ca5a399/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_513_980_647_1059.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F5e944187a7978597f737a9377089b07aefd07b3e40e09bc47d0ebc672e34a9ca" alt="Image" width="11%" /></div>


According to a report by the United Nations Population Fund published in April 2023, 68 per cent of India's population belongs to the age group 15-64, India is now one of the world's fastest-growing economies and became the 5th largest in 2022.

Recent steps by the Indian government include schemes such as Startup India and Stand-up India for entrepreneur minds to start their own business. Also, the National Skill Development Mission started in 2015 aims to empower the youth of the country with adequate skill sets that enable employment and improve productivity.

How have countries like Japan, Switzerland, and Singapore been able to achieve a remarkably high level of economic development despite their limited natural resources?

In India, more people live in rural areas (about 69 per cent) than urban areas (about 31 per cent) However, in recent years a large number of people have migrated from rural areas to urban areas in search of jobs, good education and better living conditions. This may have had an impact on the population of urban areas.

### Geographical Distribution of Indian Population

There are various factors that affect the distribution of population in our country such as physical features, climate, availability of natural resources and the level of industrialization. The population distribution in India is not even. The highest concentration of

##### Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs)

##### Goal-3: Good Health and Well-being

Ayushman Bharat is a health protection scheme of Government of India, which is intended to cover over 10 crore poor and vulnerable families, providing coverage of up to 5 lakh rupees per family per year in case of hospitalization.

The scheme will provide access to quality healthcare. It will lead to timely treatments, increase in patient satisfaction, improvement in productivity and efficiency, and job creation. This will thus lead to improvement in quality of life.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//ab09cd52-aa9d-4bae-8649-92b95e9ab5a6/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_144_52_887_1006.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A27Z%2F-1%2F%2F10e1f7751d01d50bed34a85d974e535cf71cd2b5cd51821fc0aa749f2dbffe67" alt="Image" width="62%" /></div>

#### Sex Ratio

Sex ratio is defined as the number of females per thousand males. In India, on an average, there are more males than females—943 females to every 1,000 males. In some states, the sex ratio is low, with only 879 females to every 1,000 males in Haryana and 895 females to every 1,000 males in Punjab. There are a number of reasons. Greater mortality rates of female babies and the girl child being killed at birth are two important reasons for poor sex ratio in these states.

Kerala and Puducherry have the highest sex ratio with 1,084 females to 1,000 males in the

#### Biography

John Graunt (1620–1674 CE) was an English statistician who is known to be the founder of demography, epidemiology and vital statistics. His most celebrated contribution was the creation of the first mortality table. By analysing birth and death rates, he was able to roughly calculate the male-to-female ratio, even the population of London in his publication 'London Bills of Mortality'. He was also the first to document the phenomenon of 'excess deaths' during epidemics.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//ab09cd52-aa9d-4bae-8649-92b95e9ab5a6/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_911_107_1136_320.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2F73b147ebeba4f9398a4532db4cfaee7ac9e14e982bbd9c062fabbfd9471219fb" alt="Image" width="18%" /></div>


#### Points to Remember

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//ab09cd52-aa9d-4bae-8649-92b95e9ab5a6/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_36_383_1176_1215.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2F83c5d271383fd34e5e07f2d857c61a109dab8be370e9be46d3875c3ea845d5ac" alt="Image" width="95%" /></div>


<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//ab09cd52-aa9d-4bae-8649-92b95e9ab5a6/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_87_1230_154_1305.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2F2505b3e7268f7acc9c7dd2226c17641326ede9b96ffd0dcf2583826acf453e32" alt="Image" width="5%" /></div>


#### Important Terms

Manpower: The number of workers needed or available to do a particular job

Human resources: People are considered a resource because their skills and abilities can be used.

Per capital income: Income for each person

Sex ratio: The number of females per thousand males

Mortality rate: The number of deaths per 1,000 live births

2. Study the data and answer the questions that follow.

Ministry of External Affairs (MEA) data shows that there are 32 million Indians living abroad who are either NRIs or OCIIs. Indians form the largest diaspora of migrants in the world. Indian students go abroad in large numbers. Till January 2021, more than 1 million students are studying overseas in over 85 countries. More than 50% of them chose to go to North America. It has been estimated that by 2024, Indian students studying abroad would increase to 1.8 million. The amount spent would hit 80 billion USD. This is an extremely large amount of money flowing out of the country. It also causes immense amount of brain drain because this motivated, educated and capable Indians, desire to seek equal opportunities and hence, settle abroad. This takes away our human capital, a precious resource in context of today's India and its future.

(i) What term is used to describe the situation mentioned in the above passage? [1]    
(ii) Write two causes of the situation.    
(iii) Write two impacts of the situation on India.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//c74c42ee-4246-4e79-bdc2-30397f47fba7/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_600_691_1127_981.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F70438d8dbafebe64308570a341d9fcd590e52824b4d264c3e630e6016f3f6340" alt="Image" width="44%" /></div>


2. Study the passage and answer the questions that follow.

Mangrove forests in India are vital coastal ecosystems. They are found in the deltas of all major rivers. An example is the Sundarbans, the Ganga-Brahmaputra delta. They are unique and are characterized by salt-tolerant trees and shrubs that thrive in brackish water (water less salty than seawater). They are home to many plant and animal species. They also play a crucial role in coastal protection. The intricate root system of the mangrove forest stabilizes coastal soils and protects against erosion. Also, mangroves are good at absorbing and storing carbon dioxide from the atmosphere, thus helping in reducing greenhouse gas emissions.

(i) How are mangrove trees and shrubs unique? [2]    
(ii) In what ways are mangrove forests important for coastal protection? [2]    
(iii) Can mangrove forests help in reducing the effects of greenhouse gases? How? [3]

# Worksheet 2

Read the passage and answer the questions that follow.

The Pacific Ring of Fire is a horseshoe-shaped zone that encircles the Pacific Ocean, known for its intense geological activity. This region is home to approximately 75 per cent of the world's active and dormant volcanoes, as well as a significant portion of the world's earthquakes. The Ring of Fire's geological activity is primarily caused by the collision and interaction of several tectonic plates that make up the Earth's outer shell. Along this fiery arc, volcanic eruptions and seismic events are common occurrences, shaping

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//50682dd3-1b52-4988-94be-ff8e7a900664/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_560_118_1110_490.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A28Z%2F-1%2F%2F9af1aa7b5cbbf85a1ecd83fdd1f16b57483a3f2c7bda529288140b514a23fa3b" alt="Image" width="46%" /></div>


the landscape and often presenting both hazards and opportunities for the communities residing in these regions. Despite the risks, the Pacific Ring of Fire is also renowned for its stunning natural beauty, biodiversity, and rich cultural heritage, making it a region of both scientific interest and wonder.

1. What is the Pacific Ring of Fire, and why is it called so?

2. What geological phenomena are most commonly associated with the Pacific Ring of Fire?

3. What causes the intense geological activity in the Ring of Fire?

4. How do tectonic plate movements contribute to the formation of volcanoes and earthquakes in this region?

5. What are some of the risks and challenges faced by communities living in the Pacific Ring of Fire?

6. Despite the geological hazards, why is the Pacific Ring of Fire considered a region of scientific interest and wonder?

7. What measures can be taken to mitigate the risks associated with living in this geologically active region?

5. On the outline map of Asia below, mark the climate and natural vegetation of Asia. You can use different colours. Also give the map a title and draw a legend.

# Map Practice 2

Look at the map below and answer the questions that follow.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//50682dd3-1b52-4988-94be-ff8e7a900664/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_242_182_921_751.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A13%3A29Z%2F-1%2F%2F184bb95ba1353f99904036267dcc619c928fb9d985e86c2e96aafc0e36d74bb1" alt="Image" width="57%" /></div>


1. Identify and name the countries that share a border with India.

2. What is the capital city of the country immediately to the west of India?

3. Which country in East Asia is known as the 'Land of the Rising Sun'?

4. Find and name a country in Southeast Asia that consists of thousands of islands.

5. Name the country that is located at the crossroads of Europe and Asia and is known for its rich cultural history.

6. Locate and name two countries in Central Asia that were part of the former Soviet Union.

7. Identify the largest country in Asia both in terms of land area and population.

Locate a landlocked country in South Asia and name it.
